Outside Dagu Port, Ice Mountains Block the Waterway

Ships Trapped, Supplies Cut Off; Peddlers Carry Food on Ice to Sell

Tianjin - Outside Dagu Port, the ice is solid and, agitated by the tide, rises high like mountains, stretching endlessly. Regular ships between Dalian and Tianjin, as well as Yingkou and Miyapu, are surrounded by icebergs. On the afternoon of the 5th, they risked sailing into Tanggu, sustaining multiple damages to their hulls. Navigation to and from the port remains blocked. The ice mountains between Tanggu and Dagu are piled up to over ten feet high, making it impossible to break through. Because of the accumulation of icebergs outside Dagu Port, the waterway is blocked, and imported goods have not arrived for nearly two weeks. The price of imported goods needed in Tianjin has skyrocketed. (Special Dispatch, 6th)

Tianjin - The Port Director of Tianjin Customs issued a notice on the 6th, stating that the ice in Bohai Bay has recently become very thick, and all ships traveling to and from should avoid danger, as the port will not be responsible. As of the evening of the 6th, a total of seventeen large ships were trapped in the ice outside Dagu Port, all visible outside Heigu. The number of ships that are out of sight due to the distance and weather is unknown. Chinese and foreign shipping companies in Tianjin held a meeting at the Dalian Steamship Company on the 6th to discuss rescue methods, but no solution was found. Peddlers outside Dagu Port risked traveling on the ice to sell food to the frozen ships. A pound of wheat bread was priced at six or seven yuan. (Special Dispatch, 6th)

Tianjin - The ships trapped in the ice in Zhili Bay have had their supplies cut off, making assistance difficult. Shipping merchants are very concerned. Many passengers are on board the trapped ships. A plan to use Chinese ice sleds to transport food ultimately failed because the ice surface was uneven and had breaks, and the goods being carried were also heavy. The Huogu Tugboat Company had no choice but to hire many laborers to carry coal on the ice to reach the trapped ships, but each person could only carry forty pounds of coal. Shipping representatives held a meeting here yesterday and repeatedly appealed to Dalian to send a powerful icebreaker for assistance, but this is likely to be ineffective because Dalian's icebreakers are currently busy at their own port and Huludao. However, it is reported that a certain icebreaking vessel has now arrived at Shaludian (transliteration), where three Chinese and Japanese merchant ships are in a dangerous situation. The Shengjing steamer, which left Shanghai yesterday, may load coal in Qingdao to supply the Taikoo ships, which are currently trapped at Dagu. The Wuzhou steamer is short of food, while the Hubei and Nanzhuan steamers, although not lacking in food, are running out of coal. The Wuzhou steamer sent a radio message today stating that despite repeated attempts, they have been unsuccessful, and starting the engine is just wasting coal. They only light the fire for four hours each day, waiting for the weather to improve. A Jardine Matheson ship reached ten miles from Dagu but turned back to Yantai. The Tianjin Navigation Company's Xikang steamer is currently leaking and lacks food and coal. The weather has not improved today, and the ice blocks remain very thick. It snowed non-stop in Tianjin last night. (Reuters, 6th)

Tianjin - Since the sudden cold snap in late January, the sea surface within sixty miles outside Tanggu has frozen to a thickness of over ten feet, resulting in the greatest freeze in two hundred years. As a result, Tianjin has been completely blocked by solid ice. The Osaka Shosen Kaisha's Changan Maru, which set sail on the morning of the 1st, was the last merchant ship to leave Tianjin. Currently, all inbound and outbound ships are blocked, resulting in chaos. There are currently twelve merchant ships and two ferries anchored outside the port, but all are trapped by solid ice and cannot move. All shipping companies are helpless, and icebreakers are also experiencing difficulties. Therefore, those involved in shipping, such as shipping companies, transportation businesses, and dockworkers, can only wait helplessly for the thaw. The Osaka Shosen Kaisha's Changjiang Maru, which was originally scheduled to enter the port on the night of the 3rd, has now decided to divert to Qinhuangdao to allow passengers to disembark. Due to the freezing of Tanggu, the import and export of important commodities in Tianjin have been suspended, disrupting commercial activity. There is also a shortage of food, threatening the people. This is the greatest freeze Tianjin has ever experienced since its opening. (Dentsu, 6th)

Various Locations: Snowstorms Disrupt Traffic

Beiping - Due to heavy snow last night, the long-distance telephone lines between Beiping and Tianjin were broken and out of service from 7:00 AM this morning. The telephone bureau dispatched workers to repair them, and they were restored to normal service by 1:00 PM this afternoon. (Special Dispatch, 6th)

League of Nations Studies Oil Embargo: Subcommittee Completes Report

Success of Oil Embargo Against Italy Hinges on U.S. Attitude

Geneva - The League of Nations subcommittee studying oil substitutes completed its draft report today, which will be discussed by the full committee studying the oil embargo against Italy tomorrow. The report details all substitutes and the extent to which Italy can obtain them. (Reuters, 5th)

Geneva - The committee of experts from eighteen nations, discussing the embargo on kerosene, discussed the issue of importing kerosene from the United States, Russia, and Romania into Italy this afternoon. Detailed information was collected for study. The expert committee has almost completed its study on the question of what substitutes Italy could use once the embargo is implemented. (Havas, 5th)

Geneva - Economic experts investigating the potential success of an oil embargo against Italy today estimated Italy's existing oil reserves at 500,000 to 700,000 tons, sufficient for only six months of use. Even if Italy could purchase oil abroad, the number of oil tankers available could not meet the total demand. Therefore, experts believe that the success of the oil embargo depends entirely on the United States, as the United States controls half of the world's kerosene production and has a quarter of the world's oil tankers. (National News Agency, 5th)

New York - The Oil and Gas Journal reported today that the amount of kerosene extracted in the United States in the week before February 1 was slightly less than in the previous week. The average daily extraction rate was 2,815,550 barrels, compared to 2,820,500 barrels in the previous week. The average daily extraction rate in the week before January 18 was 2,833,600 barrels. (National News Agency, 5th)

US-UK Talks on Reviving International Trade

British House Debates Redistributing World Resources; Motion to Convene International Conference Defeated

Washington - British and American diplomats are currently discussing methods to promote the revival of international trade. Secretary of State Hull told reporters today that British Ambassador to the United States Sir Ronald Lindsay has held multiple meetings with the State Department. Although the two countries do not yet have specific proposals, he hopes that tangible progress can be made. (Reuters, 5th)

London - Former Labour Party leader Lansbury proposed a motion stating that he firmly believes in the futility of war and that the British government should immediately work to convene an international conference under the auspices of the League of Nations to address the economic problems that are causing countries around the world to prepare for war. This motion was debated intensely in the House of Commons yesterday and was defeated by a vote of 228 to 137. However, the House of Commons passed an amendment proposed by Conservative MP Evans by a vote of 207 to 125, endorsing the first paragraph of Lansbury's motion and expressing confidence that the government would make sincere efforts to increase international prosperity and goodwill. Former Prime Minister Lloyd George spoke, urging the government to accept Lansbury's motion, stating the increasingly tense situation due to countries' preparations for war and saying that peace cannot be achieved until the distribution of League of Nations mandates is reconsidered.

Lansbury Motion, Lloyd George Support, Conservative Amendment Passed

Lansbury, in his motion, stated that economic issues such as access to raw materials and markets and the need for immigration are the reasons for the current global arms race. He does not believe that any system relying solely on force can maintain fairness to the enemy once war breaks out, as the belligerent nations have lost their sense of right and wrong. Solutions achieved through force will inevitably be reconsidered and revised sooner or later. We should examine the world's economic situation. He does not advocate dividing the British Empire among others but seeks a completely new concept of world unity, under which global resources can be managed by an international authority serving all countries. If governments can cooperate, this humane proposal would be easier to implement.

Evans then proposed an amendment, and Lloyd George followed up, supporting Lansbury, saying that countries are now actively preparing for war, reasoning that because other countries are extensively arming themselves, we should follow suit. The economic aspects of this issue deserve attention. He represented the British Empire in concluding the Treaty of Versailles, and therefore he feels obliged to speak. He does not believe that peace can be achieved until League of Nations mandates are reconsidered. We should inform other countries of Britain's readiness to reconsider the mandates. The hopes arising from the Locarno Treaties and the Paris Peace Pact have been completely lost in recent years. Global armaments have greatly increased, and the tense, fearful, and dangerous situation is becoming increasingly apparent. The two great powers of Europe, Russia and Germany, fear encirclement. Germany fears Russia and France, while Russia fears Germany and Japan. Can't this fear be eliminated early to avoid regrets? Economic considerations are extremely important. Japan's actions in the Far East and Italy's war in Ethiopia are examples. He does not advocate ceding a piece of the Empire, but the League of Nations mandates should be reconsidered in a comprehensive review of colonial issues. Germany's demands should not be disregarded because of the foolish words of some German leaders. He asks the government to consider whether now is the right time to convene a meeting of nations to ask what they want.

Liberal Party member Burnett stated that Lansbury's method of seeking peace is to give up everything. Lansbury strongly objected to this, so Burnett asked Lansbury to explain what he was unwilling to give up. Lansbury replied that there is nothing worth sacrificing human life for, and there are many other ways to struggle besides killing. Conservative Party member Emery stated that such a meeting would inevitably fail. How can convening a meeting and asking countries to be prepared to give up their territory or change their economic policies be helpful? Undersecretary of State Cranborne spoke on behalf of the government in response to Lansbury's proposal, saying that the government does not disagree with Lansbury's words, but the difference of opinion lies in the degree of faith only. Everyone is anxious about the state of global armaments. If Britain does reconsider the current state of its own military preparations, it will do so not to start a war but to strengthen its ability to maintain order and resist forces that disrupt order. If the situation changes and there is an opportunity for general disarmament, the government will seize it with both hands. Former Foreign Secretary Hoare made a statement on the raw materials issue in Geneva, and the government still believes that international discussion of this issue has great value. But who can say that the time is ripe for discussing such complex issues? We must avoid repeating the disastrous failure of the 1933 International Monetary and Economic Conference. The government does not want to avoid anything. Preliminary research on this issue has already begun, but in the current environment, it has not been possible to decide on the date for continuing negotiations.

After the debate, Lansbury's motion was defeated, and the Conservative amendment was passed. (Reuters, 6th)

Japan Eager to Participate in Redistribution of World Resources, In Line with Hirota's Ideas

On the 5th, the British House of Commons proposed convening a world conference on resource redistribution, believing that it is necessary to maintain world peace and implement fair distribution of resources and territory. This proposal was advocated by the United Kingdom, the United States, and France. Foreign Minister Hirota has also strongly advocated for the free acquisition of resources and markets in his diplomatic speeches in the Diet. Therefore, Japan will take the lead in participating when the United Kingdom considers holding an international conference on resource allocation, and will openly express its participation policy. (Dentsu, 6th)

London - Lieutenant Commander Ishimatsu of the Japanese Navy has recently published a book here entitled "Japan Should Fight Britain," which states, "Unless Japan ceases its outward expansion policy, Britain should abandon a portion of its ownership or its hoped-for ownership. Even if the current trade treaties between Britain and Japan are revised, it may be enough to solve economic difficulties temporarily, but it will only postpone the date of the crisis and the conflict between the two countries will ultimately be unavoidable. This is because Japan's population is rapidly increasing while its resources are scarce, leading to economic hardship. The ultimate solution lies only in the use of force. The reason why Japan will eventually fight Britain is precisely this. Britain's vast territory and abundant resources mean that even if it gives up some parts, it will be self-sufficient. Conversely, Japan's territory and resources are both insufficient, so what it is fighting for is a matter of national survival. For Britain to plan for the best, it must restrain its pride and willingly concede, which is enough to protect itself." The author also speculates that Japan may be able to cope with a united front of the United Kingdom and the United States, saying, "Since the European War, Britain has been unhesitatingly close to the United States, even to the point of humbling itself to please the United States. The fact that Britain and the United States are competing for the world is certainly true, but if a third party rises on the international stage, they will abandon their grievances and repair old friendships to cope with the situation." (Havas, 6th)

British Military Aircraft Squadron to Make a Periodic Goodwill Flight to Japan

Departing from Singapore on the 10th; Expected to Arrive in Kasumigaura on the 25th

Tokyo: The British Royal Air Force from Singapore, intending to conduct a goodwill flight to Japan, is scheduled to depart from Singapore on the 10th of this month, passing through Manila, Hong Kong, Shanghai, and Kagoshima. It is expected to arrive in Kasumigaura on the 25th. This marks the first time that a large British military aircraft squadron will fly to Japan, making it a landmark event in aviation history that has attracted significant attention. The aviation personnel will include 21 individuals in addition to the commander-in-chief, Mr. Sidney Smith. The flight route from Shanghai to Kagoshima and Kasumigaura has been discussed and agreed upon with the Japanese Navy. The confirmed arrangements are as follows:

On the 23rd of this month, the squadron will depart from Shanghai and follow a direct route between Shanghai and Kagoshima, landing in Kagoshima Bay. Departing from the south of Oshima, Kagoshima, it will fly towards a point ten nautical miles south of the Nojima Lighthouse. It will then head north along the outer side of the Boso Peninsula, entering the mainland from Kujukuri Beach, and land in Kasumigaura on the same day. On March 1st, it will depart from Kasumigaura and return along the same route, arriving back in Singapore on March 10th. This is the current tentative plan. (DOMEI News Agency, 6th)

Soviet Russia to Borrow Funds from England; Totaling £40 Million; Negotiations in Progress

London: Rumors of Soviet Russia intending to borrow funds from England have been circulating for some time. According to information obtained by this newspaper from sources related to the two countries, negotiations regarding this matter are currently in progress. The Cabinet has repeatedly studied the issue and has sent personnel to Moscow to work with the Soviet authorities to finalize the details of the loan and the collateral that the Soviet Union can provide. The value of the collateral currently proposed by the Soviet Union is only 75% of the total loan amount. Some British cabinet members are advocating for full collateral. The total loan amount is reportedly £40 million, with an annual interest rate of 6.5% to 7%. The British government would also issue an equal amount of public bonds domestically with an annual interest rate of 2.5% to 3% to finance this loan. The difference in interest rates (approximately 4%), along with approximately £15 million of funds deposited in British banks during the Tsarist era that have not been used since the revolution, would be used to settle Tsarist-era debts owed to Britain. It is reported that the Cabinet is highly supportive of lending funds to the Soviet Union to enable it to rapidly rearm and improve its railway materials. (Havas News Agency, 5th)

England to Issue White Paper Announcing National Defense Plan; Naval Section Most Important

London: The Cabinet discussed the issue of national defense expenditure this morning and decided to issue a white paper explaining the rearmament plan. This white paper will be published at the end of this month. While the official content of the plan remains strictly confidential, it is generally known that the plan for the Air Force proposed in 1934 (stipulating that the number of Air Force aircraft should be doubled within five years) will not undergo any substantial modifications at this time. However, construction work will be accelerated. For example, each aircraft factory must produce a complete set of all components in addition to each aircraft, so that a second aircraft of the same type can be built in a short period of time simply by installing the fuselage. Regarding the Army, the number of reservists and supplementary reservists will gradually be increased. The work of mechanizing and motorizing the active army is already underway, and funds will be raised to continue this work. The most important part of the plan is the Navy. It is not yet known whether the Navy will build battleships this year, but there is no doubt that the construction of one or two aircraft carriers is currently under consideration. In addition, the Navy believes that cruisers are essential for imperial defense and will expedite their construction to increase the number from the current 50 to 70, and will also build a number of torpedo boats. (Havas News Agency, 5th)

London: It is reported that the British government's national defense plan has been drafted and will be considered at the next cabinet meeting. It seems likely that the proposal to raise funds to reorganize the army, navy, and air force will be shelved due to opposition from the Ministry of Finance. The general idea is that during the implementation of the national defense plan, short-term bonds will be used in the form of treasury bills to raise the necessary funds. (Reuters, 6th)

London: The British government has decided to issue £200 million in national defense bonds to expand the army, navy, and air force. At the same time, a new organization for the command of the national forces will be established and its policies defined. The details will be announced soon. It is reported that the general outline of the new national defense program is as follows: Issue £200 million in national defense bonds to expand the army, navy, and air force. To gain air superiority, the air force will be greatly expanded. New cruisers will be built to strengthen Britain's defense lines. A new national defense control agency will be established, incorporating representatives from the army, navy, and air force. The head of the new agency will be a civilian official. Austrian Vice-Chancellor Announces; Still Holding Restoration Stance

Naval Conference Experts; Researching Definition of Warships; England Inquires Italian Representatives Attitudes

London: The expert subcommittee appointed by the General Committee of the Naval Conference continued to discuss the definitions of various warships today. The work is based on the principles decided on the first of this week, that the distinction between battleships and cruisers should be based on the armament installed on each ship, as stipulated in the Washington Naval Treaty. The definition of aircraft carriers should also be based on the Washington Naval Treaty, that is, any warship, regardless of the number of aircraft it carries, should not be considered an aircraft carrier if it does not have the characteristics of an aircraft carrier, such as a deck for aircraft to take off and land. At this time, there are two issues that have not yet been resolved, one is the displacement of battleships, and the other is whether small warships, such as shallow-water coastal defense ships, should be subject to quantitative restrictions. (Havas News Agency, 5th)

London: Mr. Craigie, an expert on naval issues from the Foreign Office, inquired about the attitude of the Italian delegation on the issue of battleship tonnage. The Italian representatives visited the Foreign Office this afternoon to explain Italy's position to the British representatives. Italy's position is the same as that of France, agreeing to limit the tonnage of battleships to 27,000 tons or 28,000 tons. According to information obtained by this newspaper's correspondent, the British side has now realized that Italy's attitude is not as rigid as France's and is more likely to compromise. Therefore, the current difficulty lies in how to reconcile the views of the United States and France. Regarding this, some people advocate the following compromise: that the United States and European countries are not in a confrontational state, so the tonnage of American battleships may be higher than that of European naval powers. The British side believes that this statement is ridiculous and there is no possibility of it being implemented, because Britain absolutely cannot accept this method, and Japan also obviously cannot agree. Others advocate setting the tonnage of battleships at around 30,000 tons, but this is also not acceptable to the United States. (Havas News Agency, 5th)

George Bernard Shaw; Ridicules America for Abandoning Constitution

United States Planning; South Pacific Aviation

Seventh; Pan-Pacific Conference

Held in California, USA in Mid-August; Far East Economy as Main Agenda

Tokyo: The countries with interests in the Pacific, including China, Japan, England, the United States, Canada, Australia, New Zealand, the Netherlands, the Dutch East Indies, the Philippines, and the Soviet Union, have held six Pan-Pacific Conferences. They were postponed for the past two years, but in view of the various economic problems that have repeatedly occurred in the Pacific coastal countries, it was decided to convene the Seventh Pan-Pacific Conference. The convener is the United States, and a specific plan is currently being made. It has been decided that the meeting will be held in California starting on August 15th of this year, with a duration of two weeks. Notices have been sent to the relevant countries, and Japan has been urged to participate. The organization in Japan that deals with this issue was originally the Pacific Affairs Research Association, but it was merged into the Japan International Association last December. The President of the Association, Kikujiro Ishii (Viscount), has submitted the matter of participation to the Preparatory Committee, and activities have begun regarding the selection of representatives. It is reported that the theme of the conference is "The Objectives and Results of Economic Policies of Pacific Countries," including the Soviet Union's economic policy, the United States' recovery policy, and other major issues of various countries. The Far East issue will be the main focus, with Japan's economic trends as the focus of discussion. Japan plans to send twenty people to attend this conference. (DOMEI News Agency, 6th)

Current Trend Seems Unlikely to Materialize; But Credit Expansion is Still Possible

What is still worth paying attention to today is that foreign securities merchants, who are more sensitive to inflation than Americans, are no longer continuing to purchase. Today, the sales and purchases from London are roughly balanced. (Guomin News Agency, 5th)

New York: New York financial circles and well-informed observers unanimously express doubts about the imminent realization of inflation, believing that the current trend will be a moderate management of inflation to seek a return to sound prosperity. Banks here are currently negotiating to continue shipping $8,480,000 in gold exports, but this should not be regarded as a harbinger of inflation. Gold exports have reached $14,523,000 in the past two days, enough to prevent the sharp depreciation of the US dollar. What is worth paying attention to now is that the trend of US government bonds is firm, which is a major anti-inflation symbol. (Guomin News Agency, 5th)

According to Babson's prediction, the payment of benefits will raise the prices of automobile and parts stocks. (Guomin News Agency, 5th)

Washington: Inflationist congressmen warned congressional leaders that they planned to begin a movement last week to pay veterans' pensions in paper money. The American labor community, hearing this, has now risen to support President Roosevelt. Green, president of the General Federation of Labor, issued a declaration stating that inflation has serious effects on the economic and social welfare of the people. If prices rise as a result, the limited purchasing power of the people will be completely destroyed. Therefore, a sound public policy should first raise wages and then raise prices. (Guomin News Agency, 5th)

Washington: Inflationist congressmen in the House of Representatives have today begun to revive the Patman inflationary pension bill. The bill was previously shelved due to the Harrison pension bill. Now that the Harrison bill has been passed, the Patman faction has decided to ask the Rules Committee to find a way to have the bill voted on in the House of Representatives. If the committee refuses, they plan to sign a petition to force the House of Representatives to vote on the bill. (Guomin News Agency, 5th)

Repeal of Cotton Production Control Law; House of Representatives Also Passes

Washington: The House of Representatives today passed proposals to repeal the Bankhead Cotton Act, the Colth Smith Tobacco Act, and the 1935 Sweet Potato Act. This move was made at the request of President Roosevelt. (Reuters, 6th)

Washington: The House Agriculture Committee has passed the repeal of the Bankhead Cotton Production Control Law, the Colth Smith Tobacco Control Law, and the Sweet Potato Control Law, but with an amendment to exempt all past evaluations of cotton production that have not been taxed. The bill has now been returned to the Senate to seek agreement on the amendments. (Guomin News Agency, 5th)

Washington: The Senate Agriculture Committee today redrafted the government's agricultural bill, preparing to submit it to the Senate for discussion tomorrow. Senator Smith declared that the bill is still based on the soil conservation plan, and stipulates cooperation between the states and the federal government, with the Secretary of Agriculture as the liaison officer. (Guomin News Agency, 5th)

British Member of the Upper House Questions; Shanghai British Police Abuse of Force; Withdrawn After Government's Reply

London: Lord Marley, leader of the opposition party in the Upper House, inquired in the Upper House today about the incident in December last year in which the British police in the Shanghai International Settlement abused force against unarmed protesting students. However, after the government's reply, the formal motion in the Upper House regarding this matter was withdrawn. When inquiring about this matter, Marley stated that the peaceful actions of the protesting students in Shanghai were violently suppressed. External Decision Officer Stanhope replied that the scenes of student demonstrations in Shanghai published in the Shanghai newspapers he had seen were substantially different from what Lord Marley said. Judging from the Shanghai newspapers, the students obstructed traffic and attempted to enter the settlement. As for the allegation that the police under the jurisdiction of the Shanghai Municipal Council used inappropriate force, he will investigate it. However, he believes that the most undesirable thing for the Council's police is to inappropriately beat Chinese people and cause Chinese-foreign resentment. This kind of action is clearly in conflict with the interests of the Municipal Council's board of directors and the people of Shanghai. Therefore, he cannot help but doubt the accuracy of the information obtained by Lord Marley. But he undertakes that Foreign Secretary Eden will conduct an investigation in Shanghai. (Reuters, 5th)

Polish Corridor; German Train Passage Issue

Berlin: The Polish government yesterday decided to restrict German train transportation starting on the 7th of this month in order to partially remedy the shortage of domestic railway income, due to the fact that German railway trains passing through the corridor have outstanding debts that have not been paid, causing disputes with Germany that have not been resolved so far. Political figures here have severely criticized this, believing that if this restriction method is implemented, it will greatly inconvenience merchants traveling between Germany and East Prussia. Although the German authorities can expedite the opening of maritime and aviation services as a remedial measure, general public opinion here is still urging the government to seek the basis for a final solution to the issue of German trains passing through the Polish Corridor, based on the spirit of the German-Polish Friendship Treaty signed on February 25, 1934. (Havas News Agency, 6th)

Nagata Assassination Case: Japanese Military Court Continues Trial; Aizawa Answers Motives for the Crime

Tokyo: The fifth public trial of the Nagata incident by the military court continued this morning at 10:00 AM inside the headquarters of the First Division. The trial proceeded to the core of the incident. Prosecutor Shimada questioned Lieutenant Colonel Aizawa regarding his thoughts on the Showa Restoration and his motives for the crime. Lieutenant Colonel Aizawa replied that the Showa Restoration lay in removing the private ownership of power and wealth by the people. However, Minister Nagata was obstructing the Showa Restoration. He believed that "cutting him down with one stroke" could create the impetus for the Showa Restoration. He further stated that the replacement of Minister Masaki, who wanted to thoroughly clarify the national essence, was evidence of Nagata's machinations. (6th, Domei News Agency)

Tokyo: The fifth public trial by the military court of Lieutenant Colonel Saburo Aizawa, who is being tried for the Nagata incident, opened this morning at 10:00 AM. Presiding Judge Sato asked the prosecutor if there were any further questions. Prosecutor Shimada then began his questioning, asking about the specific methods of the Showa Restoration. Lieutenant Colonel Aizawa answered that it would naturally arise from the principles of human evolution, and that education, culture, and everything else must be reformed according to this principle. Prosecutor Shimada asked, then what measures should be taken against those who oppose the achievement of the Showa Restoration? Lieutenant Colonel Aizawa replied that a soldier would naturally have a determined attitude. Prosecutor Shimada asked if the defendant believed that Director Nagata was an obstacle to the Showa Restoration, wouldn't it have been possible to advise the director? Did the defendant also know that a soldier who kills his superior would be charged with the crime of killing a superior officer? Lieutenant Colonel Aizawa replied that he had no choice but to take this action for the sake of the nation. Prosecutor Shimada asked if the defendant thought that the Showa Restoration could succeed immediately by killing the director. Aizawa answered that while he did not think it could succeed immediately, he thought it could serve as the impetus for the Restoration. Shimada asked, knowing that it was a crime, the defendant still committed this heinous act, thinking that the Showa Restoration could excuse him from the crime? Aizawa's face turned red and he became visibly angry, answering, "What happens to this body is not something I care about." There was a recess at 11:34 AM, and the trial resumed at 1:00 PM. Special Defense Counsel Lieutenant Colonel Mitsui, with the permission of the presiding judge, made a supplementary interrogation. Afterward, Defense Counsel Mitsui argued for public access, saying that there had been a question of public versus private trial previously, but it was made public. The Empire did not have the slightest tremor because of this. The court adjourned at 1:13 PM. (6th, Domei News Agency)

Nazi Party Leader Murdered; Germany Protests to Switzerland; Swiss Government Promises to Punish Culprit

Berlin: Regarding the assassination of Nazi Party leader Gustloff, the German envoy to Switzerland was ordered to lodge a protest with the Swiss government. According to a recent public announcement, the German envoy expressed to the Swiss government that the German government hoped the Swiss authorities would take the necessary measures regarding this case, and stated that Swiss leftists had been launching major attacks on Gustloff in newspapers for months, indicating that the case had been premeditated for a long time. The President of the Swiss Federal Council, Mudar, assured the German envoy that the Swiss authorities would take the necessary measures to punish the murderer. (5th, Havas News Agency)

Berlin: Swiss Nazi Party leader Gustloff was assassinated yesterday in Davos, Switzerland, by Yugoslavian youth Frank Furt. It is believed here that because the murderer is of Jewish origin, it is a sign of Jewish animosity towards Nazism, and there is great outrage. The authorities have now ordered that all demonstrations of a Jewish cultural nature are prohibited without explicit permission. A public announcement interprets this order, saying that the government fears incidents may occur after Gustloff's assassination, so it is taking these emergency measures as a precaution. Jewish figures here are also shocked by Gustloff's assassination, saying that this is the beginning of Jewish opposition to Nazism, and they fear that it will cause the German authorities to intensify anti-Jewish measures. (5th, Havas News Agency)

Former German Ambassador to Japan, Solf, Passes Away

Berlin: Former German Ambassador to Japan, Dr. Solf, recently passed away from pneumonia at the age of 73. Solf served as the first governor of the Pacific territory of Samoa (which was placed under Japanese mandate by the Treaty of Versailles) from 1902 to 1911. He was then transferred to posts such as Director of the Colonial Department and Minister of Foreign Affairs. In 1920, he became Chargé d'Affaires at the German Embassy in Japan, and was subsequently promoted to Ambassador, a position he held until his retirement in 1935. (6th, Havas News Agency)

Economic Matters: The Accounting Profession in China (Part 2) - Edited by Tang Qingzeng

— Xu Yongzuo

A Brief History of the Establishment of the Accounting Profession in China: The accounting profession is not only a new and emerging profession in China, but its history is also not long in Europe and the United States. Although there have been professional auditors in England for hundreds of years, the development of the accounting profession has only been about sixty or seventy years. The presence of accountants in the United States is only over forty years old. As for China, its origins are less than twenty years old, and its development is even less than ten years. During the early years of the Republic of China, the Mixed Court of Shanghai, during the era of international public administration, referenced the foreign accounting system for appraisals in civil and criminal lawsuits related to monetary debts and appraised prices. Although at the time, those who accepted entrusted cases were all foreigners (notable examples include the English accountant Snow Myloh and the American audit firm, the American Audit Bureau), the accounting system was already imprinted in the minds of the Chinese people at that time. Later, in September of the seventh year of the Republic of China (1918), the Provisional Regulations for Accountants were promulgated by the former Beijing government, and Chinese nationals began to apply to become accountants. The first person was Xie Lin, who was then the chief accountant of the Bank of China. Following Xie, there were three or four people who served in the Ministry of Railways. Later, I also obtained my certificate in the tenth year of the Republic of China (1921). There were no more than ten people in total, and among the ten or so people who had obtained certificates at that time, there were virtually none who formally practiced the profession.

I recall that when I first became an accountant in the tenth year of the Republic of China, I only received one or two commissions throughout the year. However, because I was only working part-time at the time, I did not devote myself to it. It was not until the twelfth year of the Republic of China (1923), when the stock market crash occurred and business became difficult, that I devoted myself entirely to the accounting profession. The following year (i.e., the thirteenth year of the Republic of China (1924)), I also initiated the organization of the Shanghai Accountants Association, with the aim of using the strength of the group to promote the development of the accounting profession. Soon after, associations were also established in Tianjin and other places, and the number of members gradually increased. It was then that the accounting profession in China began to establish a foundation. In the sixteenth year of the Republic of China (1927), the National Government was established, and the cultural institutions, systems, industry, and commerce of the country took on a new look. The accounting profession was able to take advantage of this opportunity to develop, but due to the progress of industry and commerce, it was still insufficient compared to the advanced countries of England and the United States.

The Current State of the Accounting Profession in China: As of April of the twenty-fourth year of the Republic of China (1935), there were a total of 1,162 accountants in China, and the number is still no more than 1,500. This number is so small that, not only is it far behind England and the United States, but it is also dwarfed by Japan's 7,000. Moreover, the majority of them are schoolteachers, company employees, or government officials, and those who can join the association and formally practice the profession are less than one-tenth of the total. This shows that the accounting profession in China has not been able to make great strides.

As for the state of the accounting profession in our country, it is nothing more than what is stipulated in Article 1 of the Accountants Ordinance. As mentioned earlier, the business of accountants should primarily be auditing, and other matters such as liquidation, certification, and appraisal should be secondary. There was originally no need to stipulate this by national law. However, in our country, when drafting the accounting regulations for the first time, it was deemed that the accounting system was a new creation. For the convenience of those who practiced the profession, regulations were listed in the law. Therefore, although the accounting regulations have been amended several times, there are still special articles to regulate the scope of their work. Article 1 of the current Accountants Ordinance contains the following provisions:

"Accountants may, upon the order of public institutions or the commission of ordinary persons, handle matters related to the organization, management, auditing, investigation, organization, liquidation, certification, and appraisal of accounting."

"Accountants may serve as inspectors, liquidators, bankruptcy trustees, executors of wills, and other trustees."

"Accountants may act as agents for tax payment and registration matters, and may draft various documents related to accounting and commerce."

These three provisions relating to the business of accountants have not been greatly changed in the successive revisions. However, what we should pay attention to is the third item, which is the drafting of documents. This type of business originally belonged to lawyers, and it is somewhat presumptuous for accountants to do it. Moreover, in foreign countries, there are few cases where accountants are used for this. However, there is a reason why this business is listed in the Chinese Accountants Ordinance. This business was added in the sixteenth year of the Republic of China (1927) when the Ministry of Finance of the National Government promulgated the Accountants Registration Regulations. At that time, in addition to my accounting work, I often answered questions about company registration and establishment registration for the companies that entrusted me. Occasionally, I would also draft documents for them. I felt that under the current situation in our country, it was quite convenient for accountants to also handle this type of business. Therefore, when I participated in drafting the Accountants Registration Regulations, I proposed that it be included in the articles. When it was explicitly stipulated by law, it became the business that accountants in our country should have.

Internal Organization of Accounting Firms: According to the main items of business, the internal organization of a firm can be roughly divided into the following departments:

Accounting Department: Handles auditing and design work.

Document Department: Handles the drafting of documents and correspondence.

Trust Department: Handles bankruptcy and liquidation matters.

General Affairs Department: Manages all general affairs.

In addition to these, in my firm, there is also a Publishing Department that handles the editing and publishing of accounting magazines and accounting books, a Training Department that handles accounting tutoring and correspondence schools, and a Service Department that promotes the improvement of Chinese bookkeeping and answers other accounting inquiries.

In foreign countries, accounting firms are all partnerships, and there are very few that are organized by individuals. Because they are all partnerships, the scope is very large. For example, the American Audit Bureau has branches in all major commercial ports around the world, and its internal staff numbers over 1,300. However, because they are all organized by individuals in our country, they cannot be as large as those in England and the United States. However, firms such as Lixin Accounting Firm and my firm both have over 30 employees. The Zhengze Accounting Firm also has over 10 employees. The rest have three or four or seven or eight employees.

Accountant's Remuneration: An accountant is a profession, so it is natural that they should receive remuneration. The standard for determining remuneration can be divided into two types: by time and by case. By time, the remuneration is determined by the length of time spent on the case. By case, the remuneration is determined by the difficulty of the case. In foreign countries, it is more common to charge by time, while in our country, it is all by case. In foreign countries, the standards set in the United States are the highest, with a senior accountant receiving 50 gold dollars per day and an assistant accountant receiving 25 gold dollars per day. In England, a senior accountant receives 5 pounds and 5 shillings per day, and an assistant accountant receives 2 pounds and 2 shillings per day. If it is necessary to charge by case, then it is calculated according to the estimated time. The amount of remuneration in our country is all negotiated on an ad hoc basis, and in practice, it varies greatly depending on the accountant's knowledge, experience, and social status. However, according to the standards set by the Shanghai Accountants Association, accountants are paid 50 yuan per day and clerks are paid 10 yuan per day. For cases, except for bankruptcy liquidation, the fees can be determined on an ad hoc basis depending on the circumstances of the case. However, in practice, ordinary auditing cases are rarely less than 100 yuan.

Conclusion: Compared to foreign countries, the accounting profession in our country is still quite immature. Given that it has a history of over ten years and is still so immature, one cannot help but sigh. The reason for this is that the general public has yet to have a deep understanding of the accounting profession. There is an English proverb that says, "A good manager depends entirely on a good accountant." This shows the thoroughness with which people in that country understand the accounting profession. However, when we look at our country, even the outstanding members of society often despise accountants, thinking that at most they are just bookkeepers. In addition, Chinese merchants are accustomed to not making their accounts public. Some even believe that hiring an accountant would only reveal their business secrets. Therefore, the opportunities to use accountants are naturally reduced. Is it perhaps because those who hold accounting certificates in our country do not start practicing immediately because they feel the difficulty of developing their business! At the same time, from the perspective of accountants in our country, they are not as skilled as those in England and the United States in terms of quality, and they are not as numerous as those in Europe and the United States in terms of quantity. State laws cannot help them as they do in England and the United States. It is fitting that the promotion of the accounting profession cannot be as prosperous as it is in England and the United States. It is hoped that our compatriots will do their best to promote it abroad, so that the public can understand the nature and effectiveness of the accounting profession. At the same time, accountants themselves should improve, making positive improvements in knowledge, experience, and professional ethics. It is hoped that the future of the accounting profession will have the hope of being developed and expanded.

Note: This article is a manuscript of Mr. Xu's lectures at Great China University, recorded by Mr. Zhou Sinan, and reviewed by Mr. Xu. - Editor

Closing Declaration of the Anti-Opium Conference

Nanjing: The entire committee of the Anti-Opium General Association issued the following declaration after the closing ceremony: The legacy of opium has lasted for over ninety years. Despite repeated calls for prohibition, it has not been achieved. This time, the government has made its greatest determination and is making its final struggle, establishing a six-year plan to completely eliminate it, without any hesitation. The members of this association, under the command of the Chairman of the Military Affairs Committee and concurrent General Director of Anti-Opium, convened a meeting in the capital on February 1, scheduled for three days to thoroughly research the case and determine the steps. Now that the meeting is over, we hereby announce three points to the people of the country: (1) The government has indeed made its greatest determination and must completely eliminate opium and drugs within six years. (2) The government will never change its six-year plan to completely eliminate opium and drugs because of a small amount of anti-opium tax revenue. (3) People from all walks of life should support the government and urge its progress so that the government's power and the people's power are combined to completely eliminate opium and drugs. In short, the survival of our nation has reached a critical moment. We hope that the people of the whole country will rise up to fight this evil force to the death, be steadfast and unyielding, and must achieve the goal. This declaration. (6th, Central News Agency)

The Truth About the Changping Riot

The Pseudo-Hebei-East Army and Security Team Compete for Defense – Both Sides Have Opened Fire Twice and Have Yet to Stop

Tianjin Correspondence: The unrest in Changping County, which began on the 26th of last month, has now lasted a full ten days. The conflict between the pseudo-army and the Security Team led by Feng Shoupeng has not ceased. It is still unknown whether the unrest will escalate. The cause of the unrest is that Feng Shoupeng's unit, the Third Brigade of the Fifth General Detachment of the War Zone Security Team, was stationed outside Chen Guan in the city. Except for a small squad of guards, all the troops were stationed at Longshan, six miles south of the city (six miles from the city). Feng's unit was originally reorganized from bandits in Yutian. When they were stationed in Yutian in the past, they caused trouble for the local area. Since arriving in Changping, they have been able to abide by discipline. The soldiers encourage each other, and they are on relatively good terms with the people. After Yin Rugeng established the pseudo-government in eastern Hebei, because Feng was far in the northwest corner, he did not accept the pseudo-order. Although County Magistrate Jing Weifan secretly colluded with the pseudo-government, he did not dare to openly resist because of Feng's presence. The Hebei Provincial Government ordered Yin to send someone to communicate with Feng. Feng refused to budge because he resented Yin Rugeng's assistance to Zhao Lei last year in forcing the unit to give up its defense area in Tangshan. As of January 23, Yin believed that it was difficult to resolve the situation without resorting to extremes, so he ordered Ning Yushi, the entire division of Liu Runyuan's army, a newly formed pseudo-Hebei army and government civilian self-governance army under the county, to march on foot through Fengrun, Jixian, Yutian, and head to Changping. Initially, they were stationed outside the city, ordering Feng Shoupeng's unit to go to Tongxian and give up the defense area. Feng refused and secretly issued warnings. On the 28th, the pseudo-army secretly contacted Jing Weifan and suddenly opened the city gate at dawn, welcoming the pseudo-army into the city. As a result, the pseudo-army directly entered the city and occupied public and private institutions and residences. It was the Lunar New Year, and the food prepared by merchants and residents for the festival was seized by the pseudo-army. Robberies occurred every night in the city. Feng Shoupeng, angered by the occupation of his defense area, was informed by merchants and residents, and on the 29th, he notified the pseudo-army to immediately withdraw from the city. The pseudo-army refused and instead surrounded the Security Team Headquarters outside Dongguan that afternoon, attempting to disarm the guards. The guards fought back, and a fierce conflict broke out. Feng's main force at Longshan also attacked the city that night, capturing and executing the son of pseudo-County Magistrate Jing Weifan. The two sides fought all night, with the sound of gunfire as dense as popping beans. Merchants and residents closed their doors and were not allowed to enter or exit. By noon on the 30th, the fighting had not stopped. Gentry and merchants in the city, fearing being caught in the crossfire, pleaded with both sides separately, intending to mediate. Feng Shoupeng's brigade headquarters immediately withdrew to Longshan, and the pseudo-army temporarily garrisoned the city. Feng agreed. On the morning of February 1, the gentry and merchants' mediation failed. Ning Yushi, the brigade commander of the pseudo-army, took a tough stance, saying that he was ordered to come, and Changping was now under his defense area, and Feng's unit must obey orders and go to Tongxian. At the same time, a certain group of ronin in the pseudo-army, serving as instructors and supervisors, supported Ning Yushi's claim. Feng Shoupeng, seeing no hope of getting his defense area back, attacked the city again on the night of the 1st. As of the 3rd, the fighting had not stopped. However, the pseudo-army numbered about 2,000 or more, while Feng Shoupeng's unit had only a little over a hundred. The advantage Feng's unit had was that it was equipped with mortars, mountain guns, and other heavy weapons, while the pseudo-army had only machine guns and rifles. Therefore, although the numbers were different, the strength was equal. Villagers and strongmen in the nearby villages had a slightly better impression of Feng's unit and secretly provided assistance. Feng is currently in a significant advantage. However, the pseudo-government has recently reported to the military headquarters, ordering them to obey the order and withdraw from the defense area in Tongxian, otherwise, the Hebei-East Air Force will be sent to bomb them (4th).

Xie Jieshi: The Bombing Case in Taichung – The Details Were Not Released Until Two Months Later

Xiamen Correspondence: Xie Jieshi, the pseudo-Manchukuo ambassador to Japan, is originally from Taiwan. When Xie returned to Taiwan last year, the Taiwan Governor-General's Office welcomed him with great fanfare. On the morning of November 28th at 8:00 AM, Xie was traveling on the Taiwan Railway flower car from Alishan, passing through Chiayi Station. When the car stopped at the station, a bomb suddenly exploded in the waiting room of the station, the sound reverberating far and wide, and the order of the station was thrown into chaos. The crowd fled in panic, but fortunately, no one was injured. Afterward, the Taiwan authorities considered the matter serious and ordered the Tainan Police Station to investigate strictly. At the same time, they prohibited newspapers from publishing the incident. From then on, Xie Jieshi's movements were also prohibited from being reported in newspapers. The ban was not lifted until January 31st of this year, and the details of the case were released as follows. On December 28th, near the Akasaka Temple in Liujia, Zengwen County, about 50 to 60 lands away from the foot of the mountain, three places were found with the same explosive gunpowder. There were about 500 men and women gathered on the ground making medicine, claiming it was the "divine efficacy" of Akasaka Temple Mountain. The police bureau used this as a clue to investigate the bombing case at Chiayi Station. After two months, it was determined that the bomb maker was Wang Chuneng, a resident of No. 355 Shanhua Village, Xinhua County, Tainan Prefecture, 27 years old, who worked as a driver at the Xilun Motor Company in Xiluo Street, Jiayi County. As a result of the detention and interrogation, it was recognized that Wang was a machinery research and invention enthusiast, and he was prosecuted on January 24th for violating the Regulations on the Control of Guns, Cannons, and Explosives. Wang's motive for the crime was that when Wang drove a car, it always aroused his inventive thoughts. He wanted to find a way to attract car customers. He cooperated with two or three friends and spent hundreds of dollars in capital. One day, Wang suddenly remembered that the Mailiao Temple had the so-called "Ling Shan Immortal Elixir," and many people went to seek it, and the motor company and joss paper store made ten times the profit. He immediately purchased electrical machinery materials and gunpowder from Chiayi and wrote spells, roughly saying, "On the fifth day of the old calendar, at the hour of Mao, Ling rice will spray out from Mailiao Temple Mountain, buy it for the common people, the rest is military advisor Liu Bowen," and posted them everywhere. He then loaded the gunpowder into bamboo tubes purchased from a firecracker shop, eight inches long and one inch in diameter, and made them on November 27th. He planned to chant spells and draw symbols in the market and then detonate them to induce superstition. On the 28th, when he carried the explosives to Chiayi Station, Xie Jieshi happened to arrive at the station, and there were many supporters. He then placed the explosives in the third waiting room, lit the fuse, and fled. The explosion occurred at noon, and the sound was like a bomb. The above is the account released by the authorities after two months, seemingly unrelated to the bomb and Xie. However, the Taiwan authorities initially promoted and publicized Xie's return, but after the bombing case, there was not a single word about Xie's whereabouts, which is enough to arouse suspicion (February 5).

Jing Yuexiu Killed by Accidental Gunshot Wound

Patrolling Back Home, the Personally Carried Handgun Fell to the Ground – The Bullet Exploded and Hit the Vital Area of the Chest – Gao Shuangcheng Temporarily Acts as Division Commander

Taiyuan Correspondence: Jing Yue, the commander of the 86th Division stationed in northern Shaanxi, died on the 31st of last month due to a handgun falling to the ground and misfiring, causing injury. People from all sides were deeply saddened by the news. Northern Shaanxi and Shanxi are closely connected, and Jing had very close personal relationships with military and political figures in Shanxi, such as Yan and Xu. Therefore, a public funeral office was specially set up in Taiyuan to handle all matters. Jing himself often came to Taiyuan to visit and stay. Recently, the military affairs of suppressing bandits in northern Shaanxi have made the relationship between Jing and Shanxi even closer. Therefore, Jing's death is of particular concern to Taiyuan. The news obtained from the Taiyuan side is recorded as follows:

Details of the Incident: Jing attached great importance to the city defense in Yulin and personally led his entourage on a walking inspection every day, which he had done for nearly 20 years. At about 2:00 PM on the 31st of last month, Jing returned from patrolling and went straight back to his private residence. After entering the room, he quickly took off his coat. Unexpectedly, a fully loaded Browning handgun was in the inner pocket, and it suddenly fell to the ground. Jing bent down to pick it up. Unfortunately, when the handgun fell to the ground, the muzzle was pointed upwards. Just as Jing bent over, there was a loud bang, and Jing fell to the ground in response. The attendants entered the room to check, and Jing was lying in a pool of blood, groaning. The guards rushed forward to help him up and called for military medical personnel to carry him to the bed and perform emergency treatment. Unfortunately, the injury was in a vital area, and the treatment was ineffective. He died at about 3:00 AM on the 1st.

Oral Will: After being injured, Jing knew that there was no hope of survival. He summoned his Chief of Staff, Ma Jinhou, and other important personnel of the division to his bedside to instruct them on matters after his death. He earnestly instructed them to inform his troops that the country was in turmoil and bandits were spreading, and they must work hard to suppress the bandits, eliminate the hidden dangers in the northwest, and serve the country faithfully to fulfill their military duties. As for the position of division commander, because Brigade Commander Gao Shuangcheng is experienced and prudent, refined in his conduct, and trusted by all officers and soldiers of the division and loved by the local people, they should immediately telegraph Mizhi County to summon him to return to Yulin day and night to act as division commander and take charge of everything.

Jing's Brief Biography: Jing, courtesy name Songsheng, is from Pu, Shaanxi, and is now 57 years old. He was a military officer in the Qing Dynasty. During the Xinhai Revolution, he joined the Shaanxi Revolutionary Army led by Zhang Feng. In 1914, Zhang's unit was reorganized, and Jing was promoted to the commander of the 4th Regiment of the 2nd Mixed Brigade of the Shaanxi Army. In 1917, he was appointed by the Beiyang Government as the garrison commander of northern Shaanxi. In 1922, he was reorganized into the 3rd Division of the National Third Army and the commander-in-chief of the Shaanxi National Army. In 1923, he was appointed by Wu Peifu, the commander-in-chief of the Allied Forces, as the commander-in-chief of the Northwest Route Allied Forces. In 1927, he was appointed by Feng Yuxiang, the commander-in-chief of the National Revolutionary Army, as the deputy commander of the Second Group Army. In 1928, he was ordered to be reorganized into the Provisional 18th Division and appointed by the General Headquarters of the National Revolutionary Army as the commander of the 12th Army of the Punitive Army. In November 1931, he was ordered to be reorganized into the commander of the 86th Division of the Army, and he has retained this designation to this day. Jing had a younger brother, Wumu, who was a revolutionary giant in the past but unfortunately died young. Jing left behind a wife and concubine each, five sons and one daughter. The eldest son is now 22 years old and recently graduated from Luoyang Military Academy and returned to Yulin. The rest are still young. The daughter is married.

Aftermath: Regarding Jing's funeral and other aftermath issues of the division, personnel from various departments of the division, in addition to handling matters in accordance with the will, now Brigade Commander Gao Shuangcheng, stationed in Mizhi, and Deputy Division Commander Li Fanhou, stationed in Suide, have returned to Yulin after hearing the news to preside over the aftermath. After Yan Xishan, the Pacification Director of Taiyuan, and Xu Yongchang, the chairman of the Shanxi Provincial Government, received the bad news of Jing's death, in addition to sending telegrams to his family to express their condolences, they also sent a joint telegram to the central government, stating that Yulin is located in a dangerous area and is currently in the midst of bandit suppression, and the military affairs at the front cannot be left unattended. They requested the appointment of Gao Shuangcheng as the commander of the 86th Division to take charge of the responsibility. Gao is 46 years old and is a fellow countryman of Jing, also from Pucheng. The strength of Jing's unit is all controlled by Gao, and he is brave and good at fighting. He has been with Jing for many years and is highly respected by the personnel of the division (February 2).

Yu Xuezhong's Governance Measures in Gansu

Prohibiting Counties from Arbitrarily Levying Funds from Local Areas – Formulating an Outline of Administrative Plans

Lanzhou Correspondence: Since taking office, Yu Xuezhong, the chairman of the Gansu Provincial Government, has been very active in various administrative measures. A brief record is as follows: (1) Chairman Yu, in view of the fact that the counties of this province have suffered repeated disasters and wars, and the people's livelihood is declining, believes that strictly prohibiting exploitation is necessary to relieve the people's plight. However, in the past, many county magistrates failed to obtain approval and levied funds from local areas at will. Although the local undertakings they were in charge of were actually needed, the procedures were lacking, causing resentment among the people. Recently, a strict order has been issued to prohibit counties from arbitrarily levying funds. Those who violate the order will be severely punished according to law, and the levied funds will be recovered in full, with no leniency. (2) Chairman Yu believes that the financial revenue and expenditure of Gansu Province differ greatly, and if relief is not sought urgently, the deficit will only increase and become unmanageable. Therefore, he is determined to reorganize it and implement the budget approved by the administrative headquarters in order to limit it somewhat. It is heard that from January 25th, all organs will have all expenses exceeding the budget suspended, so that the finances of this province will gradually return to normal. (3) In order to promote the county administration of various counties this year, Chairman Yu ordered the Department of Civil Affairs to formulate an outline of administrative plans, which are comprehensive in education, health, and defense. The outline is roughly as follows: (1) Reorganize the granaries in various counties; (2) Reorganize the scattered lands in various counties; (3) Enforce the opium ban; (4) Carry out social relief; (5) Train Baoding and strong men; (6) Reform the county government organization; (7) Implement training for county administration personnel; (8) Increase administrative expenses; (9) Protect county administrative personnel; (10) Organize land reporting; (11) Improve public education; (12) Establish health hospitals; (4) Chairman Yu believes that during the current period of bandit suppression in the Northwest, the people need a sound organization to defend themselves and achieve the effect of clearing the bandits. He is determined to train Baoding and strongmen. Baoding training centers have been established in 28 counties, including Lanzhou, to implement training in stages. The Baoding chiefs will all be trained, and it is heard that a certain section chief has been sent to Guizhou Province to conduct field investigations in order to learn from the successful experiences in Baoding management in Guizhou and improve the system.

Building the Bai Mao Sluice Gate and Water Conservancy in Various Counties in Southern Jiangsu: Zhou Zhenhua

Changshu Correspondence: The National Economic Commission has allocated 300,000 yuan to dredge the water conservancy of various counties in Jiangsu Province and prevent floods and droughts. It has entrusted the Yangzhou Water Conservancy Committee to plan the construction of a huge sluice gate at Baimao Estuary in Changshu. The groundbreaking ceremony was held on the 30th of last month. This project is rare in Jiangsu Province and is related to the water conservancy of Su, Chang, Kun, Tai, Cheng, Xi and other counties. The authorities attach great importance to it. At the groundbreaking ceremony the other day, Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi and Director of the Water Conservancy Commission Chuan Rulin personally presided over everything twice in Dongzhang City, which is enough to prove the importance of the sluice gate. It is now scheduled to be completed in eight months. After that, Su, Chang and other counties can open the sluice to introduce river water in times of drought and discharge water to the outside in times of flood, and there will never be floods or droughts. The position of Baimao Sluice Gate, its relationship with the water conservancy of various parties, and the previous textual research relationships are recorded as follows:

The Location of the Baimao River: The Baimao River is located in the southeast of Changshu County, Jiangsu, passing through Baimao Town, flowing northeast through Zhitang and entering the Yangtze River at Baimao Estuary. Its distant source actually starts from the Sandun Estuary of Taihu Lake, runs through Caohu Lake and Jialing Lake and reaches Changshu County. It is 161 miles long from Hedun Estuary to Baimao Estuary. It is close to Shang Lake (West Lake of Changshu) and Kuncheng Lake, and far connected to Yangcheng Lake and Bacheng Lake. With the connection of branches and ports, it is actually a huge flow for Taihu Lake to discharge floodwater.

The Relationship between Baimao and Taihu Lake: In the past, Wang Yi's "Records of Water Management in Wujun" stated, "The water from the southeast gathers in Taihu Lake and enters the sea through the Sanjiang River. But Sanjiang River has lost its old course, and Dongjiang River cannot be found again. Only Loujiang River still exists, and the Wusong River is present but mostly dry. Another branch flows out of it and enters the sea from Baimao Port in Changshu, which is the largest and fastest." It also says: "Taihu Lake swallows many streams, just like a person's abdomen. Baimao and Wusong are like the tail plate. Yangcheng Lake, Kuncheng Lake, and Weiting Lake are like meridians. If the tail plate is not discharged, the abdomen will swell and cause disease, and all four limbs and hundreds of meridians will be diseased." From this, the relationship between Baimao and Taihu Lake can be said to be important.

The Relationship between Baimao and the Water Conservancy of Various Counties: Although the Baimao River is not very long, its tributaries are connected and surround hundreds of miles. It has a great relationship with the water conservancy of Jiangyin, Wuxi, Wuxian, Kunshan, and Taicang. Therefore, Mu Tianyan requested to dredge the Baimao Port, saying, "Baimao Port in Changshu is the first important river in Southern Jiangsu that flows northeast into the river. It has been neglected and buried to become land since the late Ming Dynasty. In times of drought, tides cannot come, and in times of flood, there is no way to discharge floodwater. If this port is connected, not only will Changshu be free from floods and droughts, but Kunshan, Changzhou, Taicang, Wuxi, and Jiangyin will also benefit." Liu Dingyi's "Discussion on Dredging the Baimao River" also states, "The flow of Taihu Lake from Changzhou and Wuxi eastward flows into the sea through Baimao. Once Baimao is blocked, not only will Changshu become a ravine, but the waters in Changzhou, Wuxi and other places will have nowhere to discharge and will overflow and be on the verge of danger."

The Current Situation of the Baimao River: Before 1913, the Baimao River was very wide above Zhitang Town, and the water volume was always six or seven feet. After driving under Zhitang, the water volume was shallower. From here down to Maochai Bay, it was five feet six inches deep and four feet shallow. From Zhu Jiaxiang and Jiang Jiawan, it was about three feet eight inches deep, and the water surface was four or five feet. The river surface was narrower and the water was shallower. From the pawnshop bridge down, it was four folds to Qin Jiawan. The width of the river surface varied by one foot inside and outside, with a flat and slow flow. The center of the river was only two feet deep. From here down to the Baimao Gate (the former new gate), it was about one foot five or six wide and only three feet five inches deep in deep places. The new gate was less than ten miles from the estuary.

The First Major Dredging of the Baimao River: During the Zhizheng period of the Yuan Dynasty, Baimao was blocked by reeds and the stream was impassable. Zhang Shicheng raised an army of 100,000, with Zhitang as the administrative government, stationed in Shanjing Estuary, and ordered Lu Zhen to supervise the dredging, trenching its land into a port, 90 miles long and 36 feet wide. This was the first major beach in Baimao. The dredgers in the Ming Dynasty were Shangshu Yuan Ji in the second year of Yongle, Shilang Xu Guan in the seventh year of Hongzhi, Xunfu Li Chongsi in the first year of Jiajing, and Xunfu Hai Rui in the third year of Longqing. Although the results were remarkable, it could not exceed the width of 36 feet.

The Importance of Building a Sluice Gate in Baimao: The harm of tides cannot be overstated, so it is necessary to store clear water and reject turbid water. According to old rules, gates should be set up at the docks to defend against tides. In the past, Fan Wenzheng also discussed water conservancy, and he placed equal emphasis on building gates, repairing enclosures, and dredging rivers. Many people who continued to build relied on this theory, or advocated building gates and dams together to expand their benefits. The old records say, "The Baimao River has always been tortuous and winding, so the mud and sand cannot rush straight. Building a gate at the estuary and discharging water at any time, the water cannot surge high and advance, so it is very important to store floodwater and prevent droughts." This is the importance of building a sluice gate.

The Rise and Fall of Sluice Gate Construction in Baimao: In the second year of Longqing in the Ming Dynasty, County Magistrate Zhang Bo built a stone gate at Baimao Port. This was the beginning of the construction of the sluice gate. In the 48th year of Kangxi in the Qing Dynasty, Governor-General Bumbu and others奏准 修建白茆康熙四十八年。 Governor-General Shao Bumbu and others奏准 修建白茆old warehouse, and in the second year of Daoguang, the old and new gates were rebuilt and opened and closed in time. This was the increase in the construction of the gate. In the seventh year of Tongzhi, Xunfu Ding Richang founded the Baimao Dredging and moved the stone gate to the east of the new gate of Su and Chang. This was the relocation of the gate. However, the gates built were mostly collapsed and destroyed soon. At that time, the mouth of the gate was eight feet eight inches wide and the gate hole was one foot six inches. It can be seen that the scale of the gate built in the past was not as great as that of the recent times, but it was also a great project.

The Motivation for Building a Sluice Gate in Baimao: In 1931 and 1934, the Taihu Lake Basin suffered from floods and droughts, which could not be salvaged. Although it was due to bad weather, it was actually caused by poor human planning. Therefore, to quell droughts and floods, we must dredge rivers, set up sluice gates, repair embankments, and build reservoirs. However, it is difficult to carry out various projects at the same time, so we must first build the gates through the river to prepare for droughts and floods. The gates through the river are the most important in Yunzao Port, Liuhe Estuary, Qipu Estuary, Baimao Estuary, Huangtiangang, Menghe Estuary, and Zhenjiang Canal Estuary. All gates above Huangtiangang (Jiangyin and above) were built by the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and the rest were planned and carried out by the Yangtze River Water Conservancy Commission. It is now stipulated that the Baimao Gate is related to the water conservancy of several counties, so it is the earliest construction.

The Survey of the Bai Mao Sluice Gate Site: The Bai Mao River originally had an old gate and a new gate (South New and North New). However, the accumulation outside the gate was very fast and it was soon blocked, causing the effect of the gate to be completely lost. It was then abandoned. In 1914, the wood piles and the gate base solidified with sand and ash were still left at the South New Gate, but the rest of the gate base was also removed. Therefore, the site of this gate must first be measured to determine its landform and examine its circumstances. The encroachment of the tide and the discharge of internal water should be carefully surveyed before the gate site can be determined. It has now been surveyed at the curved part near the South New Gate, about seven miles from the Bai Mao Estuary. The width there is about fifteen feet, which is suitable for the average width of the river body. A new diversion river about 140 feet long will be built, and the gate will be built on it, so that the scouring of the tide can be avoided. The gate will be built outside the silt prevention, that is, the gate built will be slightly smaller than the river bed section, so that the east water can wash away the silt. The base occupies about 80 mu of farmland, which will be bought at a price in the area.

The Benefits of Building the Bai Mao Sluice Gate: The height of the gate is based on the highest tide level in the Yangtze River, and the height of the gate sill is 1.58 meters below the Wusong sea level zero point. The gate has five holes, each hole is 7.4 meters wide, the gate length is 44 meters, a bridge surface is erected on the gate, to connect the automobile highway in the future, the entire gate is made of steel and concrete, the gate is suspended, and the weight is balanced by the average weight, and a hoisting hand crank is installed to control the opening and closing of the gate, if so, it is simple and labor-saving, it is closed when the tide comes, and opened when the tide goes, to facilitate the discharge and navigation, such as the discharge of low water in winter and spring is controlled, droughts and floods are prepared, sediment is stored in the old way, and the tide is rejected outside the gate, with the power of scouring, there is no risk of collapse, and the counties in Southern Jiangsu will benefit.

Wuxi: General County-Wide Household Registration Check

The county is about to complete the general re-examination of household registration. The county government specially convened 61 representatives from the party, education, military, and police yesterday to hold a random inspection meeting. Secretary Wang presided over the meeting and resolved: (1) The county-wide household registration random inspection should be carried out after the household registration re-examination is completed. The random inspection date should be three days, starting from February 18th to the 20th. (2) The implementation measures for the household registration random inspection were amended and passed. (3) The organization of the random inspection personnel shall be handled in accordance with the provisions of Article 3 of the Jiangsu Province Household Registration Re-examination Instructions. (4) The random inspection personnel shall be assigned in groups of two, and each district must have at least three groups. (5) For the random inspection method, at least three Bao should be randomly inspected in each township, at least three Jia should be randomly inspected in each Bao, and each Jia should be thoroughly inspected from house to house. (6) If the random inspection personnel find that the Bao chiefs of various townships are doing an exceptional job or are tired of working, they should report to the county government for rewards or punishments separately.
