Local News

Yesterday, Two Groups Welcomed the German Inspection Delegation; Kopp Delivered a Speech on German Economic Problems

Hitler's Leadership of the Revival Policy Has Been Effective; the Similarity Between the Two Nations Should Lead to Mutual Assistance

According to the New Sound Society, Mr. Kopp, head of the German Far East Economic Inspection Delegation, and Mr. Rosenblum, a member of the delegation, have been inspecting Shanghai for days since arriving in Shanghai from Beijing on the 31st of last month. They are scheduled to go to Beijing again next Monday and then to Tianjin and other places. The International Problem Research Association of this city and the China International Trade Association held a tea party at the Hong Kong Road Bank Club at 5:30 p.m. yesterday to welcome the delegation. Mr. Kopp, the head of the delegation, gave a speech on "Germany's Current Economic Problems." The details are as follows:

Attendees

On the host side, the attendees included Guo Bingwen, Li Fusun, Xu Xinliu, Liu Zhanen, Li Zhaohuan, Xu Peihuang, Tang Baoshu, Bei Songsun, Qian Xinzhi, Chen Guangfu, Lin Kanghou, Zou Bingwen, Kuang Yaokun, and other directors and members of the International Problem Research Association and the International Trade Association. On the guest side, in addition to the head of the delegation, Mr. Kopp, and the member, Mr. Rosenblum, there were also the German Consul-General in Shanghai, Mr. Kleebe, Consul Mr. Bai Rende, Vice-Consul Mr. Lido, Chairman of the German Chamber of Commerce, Mr. Paulsen, Vice-Chairman Mr. Wei Bo, Chairman of the German Overseas Chinese Federation, Mr. Wiedemann, etc., with more than 120 guests and hosts in total. Guo Bingwen presided over the meeting.

Welcome Speech After taking their seats, Mr. Li Fusun gave a welcome speech in English on behalf of the association, saying: "It is a great pleasure for me, as the chairman of the China Trade Association, to welcome Dr. Kopp and Dr. Rosenblum at this reception hosted by the International Problem Research Association and the China International Trade Association. Dr. Kopp is the head of the German Economic Inspection Delegation, a senior official of the Ministry of Economic Affairs, and has been granted the title of Minister by the government. Dr. Rosenblum is a member of the German Economic Inspection Delegation and a senior staff member of the German Reichsbank. We sincerely welcome the two gentlemen to Shanghai and express our best wishes for the delegation's successful results in our country. Standing on our own position, we should provide assistance in various ways to achieve mutually beneficial results. I remember with pleasure my visit to Germany eighteen months ago, when I had the opportunity to meet Dr. Schacht, the Minister of Economic Affairs and President of the German Bank, and other government officials and banking and business circles to discuss trade relations. We came up with various possible ways to increase trade and close friendship between our two countries. I would now like to mention the main points of Dr. Schacht's conversation with me, such as that the principle of equality and mutual benefit must be followed between the two countries, and not only Germany must increase its exports to China, but China must also be able to export to Germany. Only in this way can China offset the increased purchases of German goods. I am very pleased that since my visit to Germany eighteen months ago, trade between China and Germany has made significant progress. Not only have China's exports to Germany increased, but Germany's exports to China have also increased, especially railway materials. This satisfactory trend must be promoted as much as possible. Therefore, the arrival of the German Economic Inspection Delegation in China is very important. It is appropriate for the delegation to come to China at a time when the relationship of trade understanding between China and Germany is growing, which should be welcomed by us. Although our arrival in the province (referring to the delegation) still allows us to see our economic downturn, this is a common phenomenon all over the world. If we eliminate this phenomenon more slowly, we should also remember that it has entered our country later than other countries. I don't want to waste your time. I think you are all like me, looking forward to hearing Dr. Kopp's valuable opinions. Finally, I must repeat my words. We not only welcome the delegation, but also hope that it will achieve success and results in our country," etc. After Mr. Li finished his speech, Mr. Kopp took the floor to speak.

Mr. Kopp's Speech Dr. Kopp first expressed his gratitude for the banquet and praised Shanghai's important position in international trade and finance as the gateway for Chinese and foreign trade. Then he said that the purpose of the delegation was to promote the friendship between the German business community and the commercial centers of the Far East, and to serve the governments and business communities of various countries that are interested in German trade with sincerity, such as explaining the organization of German foreign trade agencies, the products needed by the German market, and the manufactured goods exported by Germany. He said that the world crisis is most serious in the shrinking of international trade, which is mostly caused by tariff barriers and exchange controls, but the biggest reason is the result of the war, the sharp reduction in purchasing power, and the debts arising from this reason. After these huge debts are gradually paid off, trade can gradually recover. In addition to the above-mentioned natural law, there are also ways for individuals, governments, and various commercial groups to help. The commercial inspection delegations in various parts of the world are the organizations for this work, which are used to promote international trade exchange provisions to supply each other's needs. Then he talked about the problems caused by Germany's heavy foreign debt burden as a result of the war, which are extremely acute. The sacrifices made by the Germans as a result of this are far greater than those of other countries. The Treaty of Versailles had repeatedly placed Germany in an irreparable position, which was due to the Dawes and Young plans, the cessation of lending to German accounts. The organization of the national economy was almost completely ruined in 1933. At that time, the political, economic, and social situation in Germany was extremely complex. The government led by Hitler then came forward and established a policy of reconstruction and revival, which has now achieved considerable results. In addition to reaffirming national defense and establishing political independence, Germany has also implemented various projects and facilities, land reclamation, road construction, and other plans. As a result, the number of unemployed people in Germany has been reduced from 6.5 million in 1933 to 2 million today. The above-mentioned work is extremely difficult and almost risky in a nearly bankrupt Germany, and its success cannot but be attributed to the political banker Dr. Schacht. He was appointed by Hitler as the Governor of the Federal Bank and the Minister of Economic Affairs, with the sole authority to do so. Various countries have criticized the methods he used, and the most serious of them have said that his actions completely disregard the interests of Germany's creditors. However, this provision for maintaining Germany's monetary system and finance, as well as debt, is the only way to avoid losses to Germany's creditors. Under this method, Germans with foreign debt have the power to pay it off. Debtors not only pay interest, but also repay the principal, but they cannot transfer the amount repaid to foreign creditors, because Germany lacks foreign exchange. This shortage was entirely created by foreign creditors who forced the recovery of the loans in 1930, that is, various countries forced the recovery beyond Germany's economic capacity. On the German side, they only advised them to invest in Germany, such as the so-called 12 million gold mark repayment plan, which is enough to show the shortage of foreign exchange. Although Germany has been sacrificing amounts to repay foreign debts and exceeding the number of international trade since 1930, under this method and the monetary situation of various countries, Germany's foreign debt has been reduced by more than half since 1930, and it is still continuing to pay off. In the near future, Germany's foreign economic and trade position can be restored. In addition to organizing domestic chips, Schacht completely reorganized Germany's foreign trade with new methods, aiming to offset imports and exports to avoid new debts. Although the government often participates in the system, Germany tries its best to adjust the commercial relations and needs of various countries with Germany, taking care of each other to maintain Germany's purchasing power and recover in the fastest time. Under this new law, especially on the import side, there have been many changes, that is, food and industrial raw materials have been restricted, and they have turned to buying raw materials from countries that produce German products. Germany's overseas colonies cannot supply the needed raw materials, so it has tried its best to promote trade with countries that produce raw materials and need industrial products. Trade between China and Germany has more hope for expansion because of these situations, that is, under the world economic downturn, this situation has also been developing in recent years, and Germany's imports of Chinese products have gradually increased, while exports have gradually decreased, which is the opposite of the above-mentioned new method. Under the successful development of natural resources by the National Government, Germany will purchase sufficient raw materials and minerals in China in the future. In this way, the economic relationship between the two countries is very fortunate, and I wish this will become thicker and thicker, and with the similarities between the two nations, such as the losses they have suffered in the past, in the future, we should obtain mutual assistance from the commercial relations between the two countries to achieve the revival of the two countries and the happiness of the two nations.

Scheduled to Go to Beijing Dr. Kopp also told the New Sound Society reporter at the banquet that he has now decided to go to Beijing again next Monday (the 10th), stay in Beijing for three or four days, and then go north to Tianjin and Jinan, return to Shanghai via Qingdao, go to Hankou again, and then go to Guangzhou before leaving China for Bangkok, Siam, and continue to the Dutch East Indies and the South Sea Islands, and return home in early April.

Participation Rules China Industrial Federation Guangdong and Guangxi Industrial Inspection Delegation Participation Rules The organization of this inspection delegation is based on the name of the factory, and the representative selected by the factory is a member of this delegation. After paying the travel expenses, members will not be refunded regardless of whether the ship or vehicle they take is a one-way trip or withdrawn halfway. All expenses must be calculated back and forth in accordance with the treatment of other members. During the inspection period, all words and deeds of the members shall be consistent and shall not be divergent. During the inspection period, if members have public speeches, they must be published after being approved by the head of the delegation and the secretary-general. During the inspection period, all public funds shall be paid by the director of the accounting group. In order to facilitate the members' documents, the delegation may hire a secretary, who will not be paid separately, and will depart together, but their travel expenses, etc., shall be shared by all members.

Organizational System The organizational system of the Guangdong and Guangxi Industrial Inspection Delegation has been drafted by the China Industrial Federation. The candidates for the head of the delegation and the directors of each group will be determined by convening a meeting of all members three days before departure to recommend each other. Starting Today, the North China Air Route is Completely Cut Off

Chinese and Foreign Ships in Shanghai Have Stopped Going; Shipping Companies Are Busy Rescuing Ships

The spring in North China is unusually cold, and the ice is frozen to the outside of Dagukou, making it difficult for Chinese and foreign merchant ships traveling to and from Shanghai. Those who encounter danger and damage are even more numerous. From today onwards, ships from Shanghai to Beiyang have been completely cut off, which has a huge impact on transportation. The details are as follows:

Supplying Coal and Grain The British Taikoo Company's merchant ships, which are surrounded by solid ice outside Dagukou and cannot advance or retreat, include Xin Shuntian, Huizhou, Nanning, and Hubei. Because the ice field on the sea is hundreds of miles wide, they have been surrounded for many days and cannot break through, resulting in the depletion of food and coal. Yesterday, Taikoo Company received a report and specially sent the Haikou ship to Dalian to load a large amount of food and coal to the sea outside Dagukou, intending to break the ice and advance to provide relief. Now Haikou has departed from Shanghai.

Busy Rescuing Since the ice at Dagukou was cut off, the Ruikang ship of Shou Kang Wheel, a Chinese merchant ship, has been trapped at sea for many days. The company agreed with the China Ship Insurance Federation yesterday and has asked the British Zizhi Foreign Firm in this city to send a rescue ship to rescue it. There are many other merchant ships that have been trapped, and they have also contacted the foreign firm one after another these days, asking them to send ships separately to rescue them. The Zizhi rescue ship and the icebreaker ship are really overwhelmed.

Suspension of Navigation to Beiyang After the Tianjin air route was blocked earlier, there were still two places, Yantai and Weihaiwei, where ships could pass. Now even Yantai and Weihaiwei are frozen. The three major ports in North China can be said to be completely closed, which is the first time in 30 years. When the Tianjin air route was blocked two weeks ago, foreign exports could still be opened, but now it is impossible to go there. Except for Taikoo's Yuezhou wheel, which still goes to Qingdao to wait for news, from today onwards, Chinese and foreign merchant ships in Shanghai will temporarily not open the blocked air route to North China.

The French Concession Taxpayers' Association Protests Against the Telephone Price Increase

Listing in Detail the Points That Are Unreasonable; Sending a Letter to the Board of Directors for Serious Consideration

The Shanghai Telephone Company in the concession is increasing prices in disguised form, and the implementation period is approaching. The Board of Directors of the French Concession Public Works Bureau will hold a meeting on the 15th to make a final discussion. For this reason, the Taxpayers' Association of Chinese in the French Concession sent a letter to the Public Works Bureau to oppose the new charging system and listed the company's errors that do not meet the public's wishes. The original text is: "Dear Sirs, the Shanghai Telephone Company's rate change issue will be finally studied by the Board of Directors of your Public Works Bureau on the 15th of this month. At that time, it will be able to adopt public opinions widely, follow public opinion, and make a final veto to the citizens' criticism. Our association only lists the points of the telephone company's rate change that are unreasonable and submits them to the bureau for consideration. It is known that the telephone is a public utility, and its purpose is to facilitate the public. Therefore, the remuneration obtained from its business can only be limited to the minimum interest that conforms to the invested capital. It is absolutely not allowed to compare it with other businesses that generate profits, which is very obvious. Now the telephone company is applying for a rate change on the pretext that the company's profits have not reached the budgeted number, which is fundamentally wrong. This is the first point that is unreasonable. It is known that since the new company took over in the 17th year of the Republic of China, its profits have been in the hundreds of thousands of yuan every year, which is because it has invested in assets, resulting in interest not being paid. However, the company's own assets and equipment are complete. From then on, even if the price is not increased, its profit will be more than enough. How can it make demands recklessly? This is a greedy and insatiable behavior. This is the second point that is unreasonable. The balance of the telephone company's current rate is not worth mentioning. However, in view of the current world economic situation and the extreme panic, Shanghai citizens are burdened with the telephone bills paid at the current rate due to the decline of commerce and the survival. It has indeed reached the highest limit, and it is only because the telephone restrictions are generous that it can barely obtain the effect of the telephone under extreme burden. If the world economy cannot recover one day, and the Shanghai economy is always shrouded in the fog of economic panic and cannot restore the prosperity of a few years ago, then the suitability of the current telephone rate should become a problem. At this time, it is a big mistake to suddenly change the rate and extract a large amount of money, which will inevitably lead to a situation where it cannot afford to pay the fee and is dismantled. This is the third point that is unreasonable. Now, let's discuss the new chapter of the telephone company's proposed rate change, which limits residential telephones to 100 calls per month and commercial telephones to 150 calls. Beyond this, 3 cents will be charged for each call. On the surface, the rate charged per call seems to decrease, but because the number of calls is limited, it is more stringent than before, so the increase between the two is more than doubled. Moreover, according to the experience, there are more than five to ten calls per household per day for residential telephones, and all of them are like this. The number of calls per household per day for commercial telephones is always around 30 to 50 calls if the average is calculated for the financial industry and busy commercial firms. Now, one is limited to three calls and a few, and the other is limited to four calls and a few. This kind of restriction is probably not applicable to the simplest telephone users in the world. Once implemented, any user in the city will uniformly increase the burden by three to five or six times, and no one will be spared. It is already obvious that the telephone company intends to use its business opportunities to extract money. Furthermore, the ratio between the number of calls for residential telephones and commercial telephones in the new chapter is 3.3 and 4.9. The difference in the complexity of the use of telephones in commerce and household affairs is very different from the above ratio. The telephone company's new chapter creates a ratio of 3.3 and 4.9 based on unreasonable and irrational guesses, which proves that it has not taken into account the interests of the citizens at all, and the rate change is completely monopolistic and selfish, and implements fishing with exhaustible resources. It also uses the authority of the Public Works Bureau to catch turtles in a jar. If it is said that for those who make fewer calls, it is the only remuneration, isn't it just laughing at yourself? Based on all these kinds of things, it has exposed its loss of the qualifications to run a public utility. Our association is a humble representative of the citizens, and its duty is to summarize the reasons why the citizens oppose the telephone company's rate change as above and appeal to your bureau to seriously consider it when studying this issue, so as to generate a decision that is credible and meets the public's expectations, and a strong and powerful resistance can be realized. The citizens are very fortunate. Sincerely, the Chairman of the Board of Directors of the French Concession Public Works Bureau."

Post Office Mail Boat Hongxin Number Formally Received Yesterday - To Be Used Exclusively for Picking Up and Delivering Overseas Mail

According to the Datong News Agency, the Shanghai Postal Administration ordered the mail boat Hongxin Number from the Jiangnan Shipyard at Gaochang Temple. After completion, it was formally received yesterday morning without any ceremony. The ship is now docked at the Bund, off the New Customs Wharf. Details are as follows:

Ordering Process

The sole purpose for the Shanghai Post Office's ordering of the mail boat was to transport overseas mail for loading and unloading from foreign ships. As foreign ships often docked outside the Wusong estuary, or along the Pudong and Yangshupu sections of the river, small boats were needed for loading and unloading. Postal Commissioner Zha Peilin, to facilitate the convenience of pickup and delivery, specially requested the General Administration to submit a request to the Ministry of Communications the year before last, entrusting the Jiangnan Shipyard to build the vessel. Now it has been completed.

Received Yesterday

The boat is one hundred feet long, eighteen feet wide, nine feet deep, and has a draft of seven feet. Its speed is one nautical mile every five minutes, with four hundred horsepower. Its speed is unmatched by any small boat in the Huangpu River. The boat had already undergone sea trials. The receiving procedure yesterday was very simple. Only inspectors from the Post Office's Engineering Supervisory Office were dispatched at 9:00 AM to inspect and accept it. It was then immediately sailed to the Bund, off the New Customs Wharf, where it is docked. It is scheduled to begin picking up and delivering overseas mail today without any ceremony.

Local - Cause of the Weather Turning Cold - Cold Weather Not Due to Lower Temperature - Actually Due to the Stimulation of the Skin by Humidity and Strong Winds

According to the Japanese-language Mainichi Shimbun, the weather in Shanghai has suddenly turned cold recently. The reason for this is believed to be the influence of the snowfall in Tokyo and Osaka. According to the meteorological observatory, Shanghai is far from the snowstorm zone and has no relationship to it. The recent cold weather is due to the high pressure from the south of Hankou gradually moving eastward. This high pressure is flowing towards Okinawa in the south of the East China Sea, and on the other hand, it is combining with the high pressure from Korea and Manchuria. The climate is gradually becoming gloomy, so various parts of China seem to have signs of snowfall. As for Shanghai turning cold, it is not caused by the temperature dropping, but by the relationship between humidity and strong winds stimulating the skin. However, it will gradually become warmer in a few days.

Xinzha Detective Team - Solved a Bizarre Oil Theft Case - A Years-Long Mystery Solved in One Day - Iron Pipe Connected to the Underground of a Thatched Shed

The Changji Oil Mill in Tanziwan, Panjiawan Road, Zhabei, has been operating for many years. In recent years, the oil produced by the mill has often suffered losses. At first, it was suspected that some workers in the factory were stealing. Therefore, the workers were replaced many times, but no one was ever seen stealing oil. Although the Tanziwan Police Station and the Xinzha Public Security Bureau Detective Team were notified, they were unable to solve the case. There are many thatched sheds behind the factory, mostly inhabited by workers who had stopped working at the factory or were still working there. The Xinzha Detective Team, in order to solve this bizarre case, ordered Squad Leaders Bao Ziying and Shi Zuhan to lead detectives Liu Changpei, Li Guiqing, Mao Gongzhao, Shi Zhanggui, Cai Jilin, Sun Youzhi, Zhu Jinrong, and Zhang Shuwen to disguise themselves and scout around the oil mill every day. They also made friends with the residents in the thatched sheds to avoid suspicion. It wasn't until about 2:00 PM yesterday that Detective Mao Gongzhao discovered the mechanism and reported back to the Xinzha Branch Bureau. Director Liao dispatched more than ten policemen including Zhu Tao to go together. As expected, an oil tank was found under the soil in the third thatched shed behind the oil mill. The tank could hold several dan of oil and was covered with a wooden lid. There was a hole on the side of the tank, and an iron pipe went straight into the ground, passing under the factory wall and reaching the bottom of the large oil tank from which oil was being extracted. Therefore, Fan Ronggui (also known as Fan San), 47 years old, from Zaoning; Xu Guohua, 40 years old, from Taizhou; Lu Ziming, 30 years old, from Jiading; Ma Jinchang, 26 years old, from Shandong; Wang Xiao Erzi, 18 years old, from Funing; Yu Zhixiang, 26 years old, from Baoying; Yang Shengfu, 36 years old, from Gaoyou; Yin Baocai, 66 years old, from Baoying; Yan Enfan, 39 years old, from Funing; Yin Xiaokouzi, 19 years old, from Baoying; Peng Wenxiu, 45 years old, from Rugao; Xu Zhuanggua, 31 years old, from Funing; Ma Zhangshi, a woman, 32 years old, from Yancheng; and Zhang Chenshi, a woman, 34 years old, from Huaian, a total of fourteen men and women living in the thatched shed, were taken to the team. According to Fan Ronggui and Xu Guohua, the theft mechanism was set up by Wu Asan and Ma A'er, who worked at the factory. Now, both of them have fled and their whereabouts are unknown. They asked us to help, and so on. Currently, the case is under investigation. It is understood that the factory, considering the importance of the case, has called a photo studio to take pictures of the oil theft mechanism for use in litigation.

Anyone with a radio receiver can listen to the winning numbers at any time, which is very convenient. The radio stations and broadcasting frequencies are listed below: Overseas Chinese XMHC (700 kilocycles), Buddhist Music XMHB (980 kilocycles), China and America XMHA (600 kilocycles), Qikai XQHB (820 kilocycles), Jianhua XHHB (740 kilocycles).

Health Bureau Warns Citizens - Prevent Spring Epidemics

As winter passes and spring comes, the temperature changes greatly. Many infectious diseases often spread at this time. According to the Municipal Health Bureau's announcement this morning, these infectious diseases are mostly epidemic cerebrospinal meningitis, smallpox, measles, and the like. They spread very quickly and are very dangerous, especially for children. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency has learned the general details of the transmission routes, symptoms, and prevention methods of each disease, and hereby records them as follows, so that everyone will know how to prevent them.

Epidemic Cerebrospinal Meningitis - This disease is caused by meningococcal bacteria. The transmission route is mostly from the tonsils of the nose or throat. Trauma to the skull or mental excitement and overwork can also lead to transmission. The incubation period is several days to three or four days. The symptoms often appear suddenly, first with severe chills, followed by fever, often reaching about 40 degrees. The headache is very severe and often accompanied by vomiting. Sensation is overly sensitive. As the disease progresses, symptoms of opisthotonos appear. Those suffering from this disease are mostly in danger of death and should be sent to the hospital for treatment as soon as possible. Do not delay.

Smallpox - The pathogen of this disease has not yet been fully determined. The virus is often present in the contents of the pustules, so even if the pus has dried into a scab, the infectious power remains undiminished. Even in the incubation period and early stages, it can be transmitted to others. The transmission route is mostly through the respiratory system and mucous membranes, invading the human body. The incubation period is about 10 to 14 days. The symptoms begin with chills and shivering, and the body temperature rises suddenly, sometimes reaching more than 40 degrees. On the third to sixth day after the onset, smallpox appears on various parts of the body. At this time, the temperature drops, and it rises again when the pustules suppurate. Those suffering from this disease will leave scars and become ugly in mild cases, and will die in severe cases. The only way to prevent this disease is to vaccinate against it. If someone in a family has this disease, isolate them immediately. All other people should be vaccinated.

Measles - The cause of this disease is also not yet clear, but it is known that humans are almost all susceptible. The virus is often contained in the blood, tears, nose, throat, and secretions of the trachea. The transmission medium is mostly warm air and contact with patients or objects contaminated with the virus. The incubation period is about 10 days. Within the first three or four days, rhinitis and conjunctivitis appear, so there is often a runny nose and tearing. Later, a high fever develops, reaching about 40 degrees. White spots the size of hatpins appear on the oral mucosa. These are called Koplik's spots. After the fourth day, measles appear. The location of occurrence is mostly fixed, starting from the cheeks, spreading to the face, and then down, eventually reaching the whole body. This disease often causes death due to complications. Those suffering from this disease should be treated in the hospital and isolated.

Gangster Internal Strife: The Truth Behind Mutual Killing

Accusations of Uneven Distribution of Stolen Goods Lead to Resentment and Gang Killing; Criminals Chen Bishu and Five Others Attempt to Evade Responsibility

Last month, on the night of the 9th, in the gangster den at No. 63 Tong'an Lane, Maitland Road, western Shanghai, internal strife broke out among the bandits, resulting in mutual killing. The bandit Lü Zhenming was killed on the spot by gunfire, while Yang Bangjie was wounded. Subsequently, the Gordon Road police successively arrested 18 male and female bandits. After investigation, two of them were found to be innocent and released. The remaining sixteen, including Lü Zhenming's wife, Lü Chen, Yang Bangjie, Yang's wife Yang Jin, Chen Dekuan, Qian Liu, Chen Liu, Hu Zuting, Chen Dehong, Qi Zhang, Liu Huaizhen, Qian Jinshan, Chen Bishu, Qi Buyou, Zhou Buyun, Miao Diankui, and Tang Wang, were detained for further investigation. This was previously reported. Investigation by the handling detectives has now revealed that these individuals committed a robbery

in the French Concession,

stealing more than six thousand yuan. Recently, on December 12th of last year, they kidnapped a fourteen-year-old boy, Weng Jinchun, on Liaoyang Road in the Public Concession. The boy's family later paid a ransom of 50,000 yuan for his release. The current internal strife was caused by the uneven distribution of the stolen goods. In addition to charges of kidnapping for ransom, the police have also charged Chen Bishu, Qian Jinshan, Qi Buyou, Zhou Buyun, Miao Diankui, and Tang Wang with the crimes of killing Lü Zhenming and injuring Yang Bangjie. Yesterday afternoon, all the criminals were escorted to the First Special District Local Court. Judge Liu Yugui presided over the court session and ordered the six male and female defendants accused of murder, including Chen Bishu, to be brought forward for interrogation. Zhang Tianyin, the prosecuting attorney for the police, then presented the defendants'

murder process

and the facts, stating that the motive for the killing of Lü and Yang was twofold: first, Lü and Yang had not received any of the 6,000 yuan stolen in the French Concession. They repeatedly demanded it from Qian Jinshan and the fugitive Chen Daweizi. Qian and Chen greatly resented this. Second, Lü and Yang threatened to report the kidnapping on Liaoyang Road if they did not receive a share. Qian and Chen heard of this and decided to strike first. On the evening of January 9th, they carried out the killings. On January 8th, Chen Bishu and Qian Jinshan went to the Shuanglongyuan teahouse opened by Miao Diankui in Zhabei to discuss the matter with Chen Daweizi and others. It was decided that Miao would borrow two pistols from Zhou Buyun's boathouse on the Binjiang Road, and that all family members living near Lü and Yang would be moved to Route Cardinal Foch to avoid

entangling family members

and making escape difficult after the killings. On the afternoon of the 9th, after 7 p.m., the killers gradually gathered at the entrance of Tong'an Lane. First, Chen Daweizi burst into Yang's home to check. Yang and Lü were both present. Chen immediately withdrew and ordered Chen Bishu and the fugitive Wang Ganlin to enter and monitor Yang and Lü. Qian Jinshan, Chen Daweizi, and a person named Dai then rushed in. Qian and Chen each held a pistol and fired continuously. Lü was shot and killed on the spot. Although Yang was injured, he tried to resist, but Chen Bishu restrained him, allowing the others to escape. The pistols borrowed from Zhou were temporarily hidden at Tang Wang's residence on Gordon Road that day. Later, Qi Buyou returned them to Zhou, who

placed them in the river.

It was only when Zhou was detained that they were recovered, etc. Subsequently, firearms experts from the Public Works Department confirmed that Lü's death and Yang's injury were indeed caused by these two guns. The court then interrogated the six defendants, including Chen Bishu, one by one in isolation. However, Chen persistently denied everything, claiming ignorance of all points regarding the prior planning and the temporary killings. The court then ordered that Lü Chen, the wife of the deceased Lü Zhenming, be brought forward for cross-examination. She testified that the killings were indeed caused by uneven distribution of stolen goods and that Chen Bishu was indeed present at the scene of the shooting. The other defendants also gave evasive answers. As it was late, the court ordered that the defendants be returned to custody for further questioning at a later date.

Chrysanthemum Tea Prices Inside the Cars

Public Works Department

Pan Mingxun, Comprador of the PWD, Celebrates 50th Anniversary of Service

Board of Directors Holds Celebration

Mr. Pan Mingxun, comprador of the Public Works Department, is originally from Nanhai, Guangdong. His family has lived in Shanghai for more than a century. Mr. Pan joined the Public Works Department at a young age and is known among his peers for his loyalty, diligence, competence, and integrity. His moral character and enthusiasm are especially admired by his colleagues. Mr. Pan has served in the Public Works Department for 50 years as of January 10 of this year. It is rare, if not unprecedented, to dedicate half a century to serving in one organization, demonstrating unwavering loyalty and perseverance. Therefore, the entire Board of Directors of the Public Works Department held a solemn celebration during a regular meeting a few days ago to express their admiration and mark this unprecedented achievement. The directors present that day included Chairman Arnold, Directors Landmark, Craney, Franklin, Hsi Yuk-shu, Hsu Hsin-liu, Chiang I-ping, Keiller, Little, Board, Occupation, Yamamoto, and Chinese directors Guo Shun and Yu Qiaqing, who were temporarily absent due to business. Key officials from the Bureau who attended the celebration included Director-General Fessenden, Secretary-General Johnson, and Head of the Finance Department Ford. The Chairman spoke, saying that at the Board of Directors meeting on January 8, he had reminded the directors that Mr. Pan, the bureau's comprador, would be celebrating his 50th anniversary of service on the 10th of that month. Mr. Pan's service has been consistently loyal and commendable. The Board of Directors, to express its admiration and set an example, should present him with a suitable gift to commemorate the occasion. The Board of Directors unanimously approved the motion. Therefore, today, I, as the representative of the entire Board of Directors, present Mr. Pan Mingxun with a clock engraved with the record of the event as a permanent memento. The directors then congratulated Mr. Pan, who humbly thanked them one by one. Afterwards, Arnold briefly recounted the beginning and end of Mr. Pan's service in the Bureau, saying that today's celebration is not only a commemoration of Mr. Pan's 50th year of public service but also a celebration of the Pan family's relationship with the Bureau for more than 75 years. A report of Public Works Department in 1886 contained a memorial of the death of Mr. Pan Yuming, which stated, "Mr. Yuming served in the Bureau for more than 25 years. He was diligent in his work and highly regarded by his colleagues." Because of Mr. Yuming's meritorious service, after his death, his son, Mr. Juxuan, succeeded him as the comprador of the Public Works Department. Mr. Juxuan retired in 1930, when he was 71 years old, having served in the Bureau for 48 years. Therefore, at a meeting of the Board of Directors on June 11 of that year, the Chairman, on behalf of the entire Board of Directors, presented Mr. Juxuan with a gold plate engraved with the record of the event as a memento. In his speech, he praised Mr. Juxuan's selfless spirit and his significant contributions to the harmony between Chinese and foreign residents in Shanghai. After Mr. Juxuan's retirement, his younger brother, Mr. Mingxun, succeeded him as the comprador, who is the subject of today's 50th anniversary celebration. Mr. Mingxun is 68 years old this year. Although his hair is white, he is energetic and healthier than a young man. He comes to the Bureau to work every day, regardless of the weather. It is truly a sign of longevity. It is expected that he will continue to serve in the future and that the relationship between the Pan family and the Bureau will continue indefinitely. There are also Pan family members working in the General Accounting Office of the Public Works Department, including Pan Shiju, the son of Mr. Juxuan, and Pan Shiqi and Shishen, the sons of Mr. Mingxun. It is also heard that Mr. Pan Jingshan, the clan elder of Mr. Mingxun, was also the comprador of the Public Works Department more than 75 years ago. Therefore, although there are no detailed records of this, it is not an exaggeration to say that since the establishment of the Public Works Department on the banks of the Huangpu River, the position of comprador has been held by the Pan family, generation after generation. In this changing world, the titles of the Board of Directors of the Public Works Department have been changed countless times over the past century, and the personnel changes in the offices of the Secretary-General and the Finance Department have also been countless times, but the relationship between the Pan family and the Bureau has been maintained continuously. This is truly a good story of Spring and Autumn.

It is rumored that the Polish Embassy plans to invite film stars Hu Die, Gu Lanjun, and others to attend, promising a lively event.

Ningbo Native Association

Writes to Four Companies, Urging Them to Cancel Fare Increase on Shanghai-Ningbo Route

Increasing Shipping Costs is a Suicidal Policy; Reducing Shipping Costs to Revive Commerce

According to Shenshi News Agency, the Taikoo, Sanbei, Ningshao, China Merchants, and other shipping companies that operate on the Shanghai-Ningbo route with ships such as the Xinjiangtian, citing the recent increase in the price of coal, metals, and other materials and the increased expenditure, uniformly increased fares by 20% on the 1st of this month to maintain the status quo. After the public announcement in the newspapers, Ningbo businesses, citing the depression and sluggish business, asked how they could bear the increased burden and requested the Ningbo Chamber of Commerce to ask the Shanghai Ningbo Native Association to negotiate with the Taikoo and other companies to cancel the 20% fare increase to maintain cargo transport. The association, upon learning of the situation, sent letters to the Shanghai Taikoo Company, the Ningshao Company, the Sanbei Company, and the China Merchants Bureau yesterday. The original letter stated, "Regarding the letter from the Ningbo Chamber of Commerce stating, 'Regarding the letter from the Yinxian Silk and Cloth Industry Association stating, recently, members of our association have come to the association to state that, according to reports, the Xinjiangtian and other four ships operating on the Shanghai-Ningbo route have increased cargo transport fares by 20% from February 1st. We are shocked to read this. Ningbo is a transshipment port. Affected by the sluggish market in recent years, business has declined to the extreme. In addition, last year's financial turmoil shook the ponds, and credit was extremely tight. The state of real buying has become even more stagnant. Businesses have declared bankruptcy one after another due to sluggish business and poor circulation, which is an undeniable fact. Now, although they are still struggling to maintain the status quo, they may not be able to maintain it for long. The four shipping companies should understand the business situation and reduce shipping costs to seek the revival of the Ningbo market, but they have not done so. Instead, they have proposed to increase shipping costs. Members cannot approve of it. Please ask your association to ask the Ningbo Chamber of Commerce to ask the companies to cancel the fare increase immediately to maintain business, etc.' Based on this, the decline in commerce and the depletion of finance, it is already difficult for each industry to maintain the status quo, and it seems inappropriate to increase shipping costs suddenly. According to the aforementioned situation, we hereby request your association to quickly forward a letter to the Ningbo China Merchants Bureau, Ningshao, Sanbei, Taikoo, and other four shipping companies to cancel the fare increase immediately to maintain business and hope to see a reply, etc. Because of the decline in Ningbo in recent years and the depletion of finance, it is already difficult to maintain the status quo. If shipping costs are increased, cargo transport will inevitably stagnate, resulting in a lose-lose situation. We hope that the government will understand the business situation and cancel the fare increase immediately to maintain business and benefit cargo transport, etc., and send letters to the Ningbo China Merchants Bureau and other four shipping companies for review and reply. While the matter was being handled, the Qin County Customs Broker Association also sent a letter with the same content, stating that the matter of increasing cargo costs is directly related to the industries in this port and requested that letters be sent to each trade association for notification. It was also submitted to the fifth meeting of the Executive Committee on February 1 for detailed discussion. It was unanimously agreed that, according to the report, the four shipping companies' announcement stated that the reason for the increase in cargo costs was the increase in the price of coal, metals, and other materials and the increased expenditure of the ships. However, in recent years, the price of coal has been decreasing day by day. Recently, the best coal has been reduced by 60% compared to before January 28. As for metal materials, they were originally necessary for repairs, but each company only repairs ships once a year, and even if there are ups and downs, it is irrelevant to the overall situation. To point to increased expenditure is not in accordance with the facts." In addition, Ningbo is a transshipment port. Since the opening of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, merchants from Hangzhou, Jiaxing, and Huzhou have mostly purchased goods directly from Shanghai. Ningbo cargo transport has already been hit. With the opening of the Hangzhou-Jiangxi Railway, the sales areas of Jinhua, Quzhou, and Yanping were also seized. Ningbo's commerce is declining like a river going downhill, and there is no way to save it. The shipping companies, at this time of declining cargo transport, did not think of ways to attract it. Instead, they wanted to increase shipping costs to compensate for it, which is the same as scaring away fish in the deep or scaring away birds in the industry. If each industry has no profit to be made, it will not be willing to transport it. If each shipping company goes back and forth between Shanghai and Ningbo, cargo transport is its lifeblood. If cargo transport disappears, it may not be able to maintain the status quo and all will die together. It is painful to say. Commentators point to the decision of the four shipping companies to increase shipping costs as a suicidal policy. It is certainly not an excessive statement. However, the proposal to increase shipping costs was decided by the Shanghai four shipping companies' headquarters, and the Ningbo branch companies cannot solve it. It is proposed that the Shanghai Native Association negotiate nearby and find a way to cancel it to maintain business. It was decided that a statement of reasons should be sent to the Shanghai Native Association to negotiate with the four shipping companies nearby as soon as possible to cancel the proposal to increase shipping costs to maintain business and send letters to the Ningbo four shipping companies for review, etc., and unanimously passed and recorded. In addition to sending letters, we hereby record the case and send it to your association for review. We hope that you will negotiate with the four shipping companies' headquarters nearby as soon as possible to cancel the proposal to increase shipping costs to benefit cargo transport and maintain the status quo. We sincerely hope to see a reply. Therefore, we specially copy the original letter and send it to you. We hope that you will take note of the cancellation of the fare increase to maintain cargo transport and ensure the status quo. We are deeply grateful and hope to see a reply.

Sino-Japanese

Telephone Service Preparation Completed; Telephone Service to be Available on the 15th

According to the Central News Agency, all procedures for the International Telecommunications Bureau's preparation for Sino-Japanese telephone service have been completed, and the official service will begin on the 15th of this month. The reporter visited Deputy Director Bao Keyong yesterday, who said that the preparation procedures have been completed. If there are no accidents, telephone service should be available on the 15th. The cost is calculated in three-minute increments, with a price of 15 yuan and an extension of one minute for 5 yuan. It will be transmitted by the Zhenru Radio Station, and users can use it directly by telephone, which is very convenient. In addition, Sino-British telephone service is also being prepared and is being tested from time to time. The date of implementation has not yet been determined. The reporter also asked about the rumor that the International Telecommunications Bureau would be merged into the Telegraph Bureau and the International Radio Station in March or April. It was said that this has only been seen in the newspapers and that no clear order has been received from the Ministry of Communications.

Shanghai Municipal National Products Year Association

Sets Work Outline and Implements it in Stages

The Shanghai Municipal National Products Year Movement Committee has submitted a request to the municipal party and government agencies, requesting that all staff members uniformly use domestic products to promote them, and has formulated a work outline for implementation in stages. The details are as follows:

Civil Servants Asked to Use Domestic Products The Shanghai Municipal National Products Year Committee submitted a request to the municipal party and government agencies yesterday, "For submitting a request to instruct civil servants to uniformly use domestic products to promote them. This year is the officially designated Municipal National Products Year. If we want to stimulate all citizens to uniformly use domestic products, it will not be effective without the promotion of civil servants first. In order to arouse all sectors to work hard to promote domestic products, the second meeting of the council of directors resolved that all staff members of this association, starting from today, should use domestic products for all daily necessities and clothing. In addition, we are submitting a request to the party and government agencies to instruct all civil servants to purchase domestic products to promote them. We hereby submit this request for review and approval, and we hope that it will be adopted and implemented."

Formulate an Outline and Implement it in Stages The association has now formulated a ten-point work outline for implementation in stages, starting on the 15th of this month. The outline is as follows: Post slogans throughout the city to promote the concept of using domestic products among citizens. Hold mobile exhibitions of domestic products in the five districts of the city: east, south, west, north, and central. Organize domestic product promotion teams, with ten people per team, to promote in both local and foreign areas. Invite celebrities from the party, government, business, academic, and industrial circles to broadcast on the radio weekly. Have staff visit the local area to inspect the performance of domestic product promotion in various stores. Hold a domestic product promotion meeting in the local area once a month. Have staff investigate the products and economic status of domestic product factories in the local area. Organize domestic product lecture teams. Publish domestic product publications. Conduct domestic product statistics.

General Situation of the Public Concession Volunteer Corps Last Year

British and American youths are gradually declining; reserve plans are difficult to implement; the Russian unit's strength is noteworthy.

According to the 1935 report of the Shanghai Municipal Council Volunteer Corps, the most noteworthy issue currently facing the corps is the problem of replenishing new recruits. The number of Volunteer Corps members in the concession is approximately between 1,950 and 2,100. Previously, the number of veterans retiring annually and new recruits joining generally offset each other, so the total number could be maintained. In the spring of this year, the corps planned to establish reserve units in each unit. Personnel indispensable to major commercial firms would be assigned to the reserve units during mobilization. Because these reserve unit soldiers are important employees of commercial firms, they would not be lightly mobilized except in the final emergency or when temporarily replacing other non-essential employees. However, after these important employees are assigned to the reserve units, their original vacancies must be filled by recruiting new soldiers. Last year, the Chairman of the Municipal Council sent a letter to various British and American commercial firms in the port, requesting their support. Subsequently, commercial firms from other countries in the area also received these letters. The responses from the commercial firms were very satisfactory, but the number of new recruits was small, making it impossible to implement the plan to establish reserve units. Fortunately, since the issuance of this request, the corps has been able to prepare a list of important employees. This list is constantly being updated and can be used as a basis for reassigning personnel during mobilization.

Furthermore, the age problem is also extremely difficult. Even considering the special police and the British and American members of the corps, it is evident that the number of youths of suitable age in the port who can join the Volunteer Corps is very limited. Moreover, the number of foreign employees in various commercial firms has been reduced, and those laid off are mostly younger. The number of young Westerners coming to Shanghai is also declining. If the current number of corps members can be maintained, the duties will not be abandoned. However, the soldiers in the British and American units cannot be said to be all young. Therefore, it is predicted that if young recruits cannot come in a steady stream, the old soldiers in the corps will eventually become old, lose their previous interest in the Volunteer Corps, and apply for retirement. The ranks will become empty. This phenomenon is expected to occur around 1939. The solution lies in the restoration of the market and the continuous arrival of foreign youths. Therefore, the current authorities in charge of the Volunteer Corps are unwilling to mobilize all corps members to the front lines during mobilization and are unable to abandon their cautious attitude when recruiting older new soldiers.

Among the Volunteer Corps, only the Russian unit has no difficulty in recruiting, and there are often surplus people waiting to be filled. Officers can select from them, and those who come to apply are generally strong and their level of knowledge has improved compared to before. If necessary, recruiting another battalion would not be difficult. According to the report of the Russian unit officers, the Russian unit in the corps is the first line of reserves for the Public Concession Police Force. Its organization includes a battalion headquarters managing three companies of soldiers, plus a company of volunteer soldiers, forming a "Class C Battalion." This type of Russian Volunteer Corps is a powerful defensive weapon in the port and can be rapidly deployed at any time. Except for large-scale internal disturbances or external invasions, mobilizing the Russian infantry unit can eliminate the need for full mobilization of the Volunteer Corps, and the port's commerce will not be interrupted. Even in times of peace, the unit's duties are very numerous. For example, when important figures from various countries arrive in or depart from Shanghai, the Volunteer Corps' Russian unit provides the honor guard. Other places such as the Ward Road Gaol, the Rifle Range, and the Edinburgh Road Barracks are also guarded by the Volunteer Corps' Russian unit.

Regarding training, several field exercises were held this year in Hongkou Park and quiet streets. Routine exercises focused on riot control. The annual shooting competition was very disciplined and the results were above average. Due to the cooperative guidance of the Commissioner of Police, the Volunteer Corps can assist the police force in the event of serious internal disturbances. This year, a plan for food transportation during mobilization has been drafted, and a book titled "Shanghai Volunteer Corps Strategy" has been produced. The book contains training knowledge from formal armies and is adapted to the local conditions of the port, making it a very valuable work.

Totaling 800 Yuan for the Whole Year

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce again submits to the Ministry of Finance, requesting to maintain the fineness of silver used by silverware shops.

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday submitted another request to the Ministry of Finance, requesting to maintain the existing fineness of silver used by the silverware industry. The submission stated (abridged): Upon investigation, the public association stated that switching to chemical silver or synthetic silver poses two major difficulties: worker skills and customary practices. Both are real situations. Leaving aside the issue of customary practices, the technical skills of the workers are a fundamental obstacle. These workers are accustomed to manual methods, and their manufacturing sites lack boiler equipment. Following the instructions of the Ministry would render the existing workers and equipment useless, requiring the addition of new machines and the recruitment and training of new workers. Regardless of the capital scale of the silverware shops, most would be unable to update their equipment and would inevitably be eliminated. The entire workforce, which has adhered to traditional methods for decades, would face the tragic fate of unemployment, fundamentally undermining the industry's request to preserve livelihoods. Therefore, after repeated deliberations, the association must appeal to the Ministry for some flexibility. Furthermore, there is no profit to be made from the private smuggling of silver ornaments, as detailed in the forwarded document to the Ministry on November 25 of last year. Once the nation faces an emergency, the people can offer their hidden ornaments for military use, as demonstrated by the example of Italy, which would not conflict with the national policy of preserving silver. Therefore, the association again submits a detailed written request, hoping that the Ministry will review and approve the public association's request, as it is in the public interest.

Instructions from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce: Method for Affixing Stamps to Housing Tickets

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce recently replied to the Southeast Construction Company, instructing on the method for affixing stamps to housing tickets. The letter stated: We received your letter of the 5th of this month, inquiring about the method of affixing stamps to housing tickets. According to the Ministry of Finance's instructions on December 31 of last year, lease documents specifically refer to leases established by tenants when renting houses. If the monthly rent is less than 10 yuan, it is exempt from stamping. If it is 10 yuan or more, a 2-cent stamp should be affixed. Housing tickets used by landlords to collect rent should be stamped as silver receipt. The rental agreement does not apply. Therefore, according to the above ministerial instructions, housing tickets should be stamped as silver receipts: 1 cent for a monthly rent of 3 yuan or more, 2 cents for 10 yuan or more, and 3 cents for 100 yuan or more.

The Grains, Oil Cakes Industry Again Calls for Abolition of Provincial Surtaxes on Flour

The case of the grains and oil cakes industry's struggle against Guangdong Province's surtax on flour has lasted for half a year since August of last year. After the Fifth National Congress and other bodies advised oil factories in various regions to resume operations first, Guangdong Province has not yet complied with the order to abolish the surtax. Yesterday, another telegram was sent calling for its abolition. The original telegram is recorded below: To Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, Director Qu of the Finance Department of Guangdong: We are writing regarding the request to Guangdong Province to abolish the surtax on domestic flour for the construction of Sun Yat-sen University. It has been half a year since the telegram. The sound is so desperate. Since the Fifth National Congress approved orders for oil factories in various regions to resume work, it has been over two months. The goods are backed up, the monetary basis is blocked, the pain felt is really indescribable. A letter was recently received from the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, which indicated the Guangdong Provincial Government had already submitted to the Southwest Political Affairs Committee for review. The surtax on domestic flour was originally collected for the construction of Sun Yat-sen University. Now the construction fund for Sun Yat-sen University has already been resolved by the First Plenary Session and will be allocated separately by the government. Therefore, the abolition of this surtax is not obstructed by any facts. Manufacturers and transporters from various regions are looking forward to the early issuance of the abolition order, which is almost like looking at the rainbow in a severe drought. Use non-speech to call, the length of the telegram, to approve the compassionate business, to turn Guangdong Province Finance Department, according to the situation, to discuss the Southwest Political Affairs Committee, and quickly issue an order to abolish it. Shanghai Municipal Grains and Oil Cakes Industry Association Gu Xinyi, Oil Factory Industry Association Zhu Jingan. Another letter from the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to the Grains and Oil Cakes Industry Association: Dear Sirs, on the 11th of this month, we received your letter, requesting us to forward a telegram to Zou Xiaochang, the Financial Commissioner of the Guangdong Provincial Government of the Southwest Political Affairs Committee, urging him to stop collecting the flour surtax. We already sent the telegram and submitted the letter. On the 28th of this month, we received an official telegram from Qu Hao, the Financial Commissioner of Guangdong Province: Regarding the collection of surtax on flour fertilizer for the construction of Sun Yat-sen University, this office is carrying it out under orders. Without an explicit order to abolish it, this office must comply. The Provincial Government already submitted to the National Government's Southwest Political Affairs Committee on January 11, 25th year, No. 49. The Financial Department was instructed to review and submit for approval. This has already been done. Please wait patiently for the review and approval.

Post Office Notice: Schedule of Fees for Overseas Mail

Central News Agency: Shanghai Postal Administration Notice No. 1290: It has been found that from February 1 of this year, all fees for mail, parcels, and airmail sent overseas have been revised as follows. Please notify the cooperation units. This notice.

Details:

1. Schedule of Fees for Various Types of Mail: 2. Overseas Column

Third-Class: Countries of the Postal Union

Ordinary Fees

(1) Letters: Every initial weight of 20 grams or any fraction thereof is changed from 20 cents to 25 cents.

(2) Letters: Every additional weight of 20 grams or any fraction thereof is changed from 12 cents to 15 cents.

(3) Postcards: Single is changed from 12 cents to 15 cents.

(4) Postcards: Double (i.e., with a reply card) is changed from 24 cents to 30 cents.

(5) Newspapers: Every 50 grams are changed from 4 cents to 5 cents.

(6) Books, Printed Matter: Every 50 grams are changed from 4 cents to 5 cents.

Trade documents and the like (but trade documents start at 20 cents changed to starting with 25 cents)

Printed documents used by the blind

(7) Documents with raised markings or convex dots: Every 2 kilograms is changed from 2.5 cents to 3 cents.

Samples

(8) Samples: Every 50 grams are changed from 4 cents to 5 cents (each item starts at 8 cents changed to starting with 10 cents).

Special Fees

(1) Registered Mail: Changed from 20 cents to 25 cents.

(2) Registered Express Mail: Changed from 60 cents to 75 cents.

(3) Ordinary Express Mail: Changed from 40 cents to 50 cents.

(4) Insured Letters: An insurance fee is charged for every 300 gold francs insured or any fraction thereof, changed from 40 cents to 50 cents.

(5) Insured Boxes: An insurance fee is charged for every 300 gold francs insured or any fraction thereof, changed from 40 cents to 50 cents. In addition, a postage fee is charged for every 50 grams, changed from 16 cents to 20 cents (postage starts at 80 cents changed to starting with 1 yuan), and a registration fee is added.

(6) Collect on Delivery: The fixed fee per item is changed from 40 cents to 50 cents. Other Fees

(1) Return Receipt: Per item, changed from 20 cents to 25 cents.

(2) Inquiry or Reissue of Return Receipt: Per item, changed from 40 cents to 50 cents.

(3) Withdrawal or Change of Address: Per item, changed from 40 cents to 50 cents. The handling fee for changing the address of insured mail via telegram is changed from 40 cents to 50 cents.

(4) Change of Collect on Delivery Amount: Per item, changed from 40 cents to 50 cents. "Per item, the collect on delivery amount is 40 cents. If a telegram is required, a telegram fee must be charged in addition to the handling fee of 40 cents," etc. The "40 cents" should be changed to "50 cents".

Fourth-Class: Japan, Korea, Kwantung Leased Territory, Taiwan

Ordinary Fees

(1) Documents used by the blind: Same as Third-Class

Special Fees

(1) Collect on Delivery: Same as Third-Class

Other Fees

(1) Withdrawal or Change of Address: Same as Third-Class

(2) Change of Collect on Delivery Amount: Same as Third-Class

Fifth-Class: Hong Kong, Macau

Special Fees

(1) Insured Letters: An insurance fee is charged for every 300 gold francs insured or any fraction thereof, changed from 40 cents to 50 cents.

(2) Insured Boxes: An insurance fee is charged for every 300 gold francs insured or any fraction thereof, changed from 40 cents to 50 cents. In addition, a postage fee is charged for every 50 grams, changed from 16 cents to 20 cents (postage starts at 80 cents changed to starting with 1 yuan), and a registration fee is added.

Other Fees

(1) Withdrawal or Change of Address: Same as Third-Class and Fourth-Class

2. International Parcel Postage List

(1) On the International Parcel Postage List, from page 2 to page 153, the fees for parcels sent overseas from No. 1 to No. 191 should be increased by 25%, except for the fees for the countries listed in Section 2 below.

(2) The fees for all parcels sent to the following United States Philippine Islands and other US colonies or forwarded via the United States should be increased by one-fifth, detailed as follows:

Page 20, No. 26: Honduras

Page 40, No. 54: Costa Rica

Page 40, No. 55: Republic of Cuba (Parcel service via the United States is temporarily suspended)

Page 68, No. 89: Guatemala

Page 72, No. 94: Honduras Republic East Coast and West Coast

Page 94, No. 120: Mexico

Page 102, No. 111: Nicaragua

Page 112, No. 143: Philippine Islands

Page 122, No. 155: El Salvador

Page 146, No. 184: United States

Page 146, No. 185: US Colonies

Page 146, No. 185A: Panama Canal Zone

(3) The original text in the insurance fee column on pages 3 to 153 of the list should be changed to: A fee of 50 cents will be charged for every 300 yuan in national currency (300 gold francs) insured or any fraction thereof. However, the insurance fee for parcels sent to Japan and other places listed in No. 103 on page 81 should remain unchanged.

(4) The amount of insurance specified in the insurance amount limit column on pages 3 to 153 of the list should be increased by 25%, except for those sent to Japan and other places listed in No. 103 on page 81, which do not need to be changed.

(5) The additional fees that should be charged for each parcel in addition to international postage at the top of pages 3 to 153 of the list (except for those sent to No. 45 Canada, No. 95 Hong Kong, No. 103 Japan/Korea/Kwantung Leased Territory/Taiwan, No. 110 Macau, No. 143 Philippine Islands, No. 184 United States, No. 185 US Colonies, and No. 185A Panama Canal Zone) are originally set at "1 yuan 08 fen Canadian currency (equivalent to 1 franc 35 centimes) for parcels weighing 1 kilogram, 1 yuan 40 fen Canadian currency (equivalent to 1 franc 75 centimes) for parcels weighing 1 kilogram to 5 kilograms, and 2 yuan 20 fen Canadian currency (equivalent to 2 francs 75 centimes) for parcels weighing 5 kilograms to 10 kilograms." They should now be changed to "1 yuan 35 fen Canadian currency (equivalent to 1 franc 35 centimes) for parcels weighing 1 kilogram and 1 yuan 75 fen Canadian currency (equivalent to 2 francs 75 centimes) for parcels weighing 1 kilogram to 5 kilograms."

3. International Airmail

For international airmail sent overseas, in addition to paying sufficient international ordinary postage, all international airmail fees charged in addition (details can be inquired at the post office) should be increased by 25%. However, domestic airmail fees do not need to be changed. Zha Peilin, Director of the Shanghai Postal Administration, February 1st

The Cigarette Industry in Shanghai (3)

— Compiled by China Credit Information

(No. 12 of the General Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce)

3. The Decline of the Cigarette Industry in Shanghai

In the first section of this article, it was mentioned that since the 17th year of the Republic of China (1928), the national cigarette industry has been declining due to increased taxes, dumping of foreign goods, and other factors. In the first half of last year, the Ministry of Finance's ban on cigarette prize promotions made it even more difficult for Chinese cigarette factories to compete with foreign businesses. As a result, the output of various factories (referring to the country as a whole) decreased due to the shrinking sales. According to a report from the Tax Bureau of the Ministry of Finance, in January of last year, the number of cases cleared from the warehouses of cigarette factories in the three eastern provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui (most of which are in Shanghai) was 68,619.4 cases. In June, this decreased to 51,984.4 cases. The rate of decrease for Chinese cigarette factories was even greater than that of foreign businesses. Detailed information can be found in the table below:

Table of Changes in the Percentage of Output of Chinese and Foreign Cigarette Factories in the Eastern Region (Year 24 [1935])

From the table above, we can see the tenacious power of foreign businesses. At the same time, we also know that in addition to manufacturing in China, foreign businesses also import large quantities of cigarettes from overseas, expanding the scope and intensity of their dumping. According to customs statistics, cigarette imports in the past three years are shown in the following table (unit: yuan):

The increasing burden of unified taxes is a major reason for the national cigarette industry's decline. In theory, the impact of increased taxes should be the same for both Chinese and foreign cigarette factories. However, in reality, there are significant differences. The products of foreign businesses are mostly higher-end and more valuable, while Chinese cigarettes are mostly the opposite. However, in the past, the tax rates for more expensive products were relatively lower than those for lower-priced products, so Chinese businesses were often more heavily affected by the increased unified taxes than foreign businesses. To clarify this point, we will compare three foreign cigarette brands—Fairy, Front Gate, and Clic—with three Chinese cigarette brands—Golden Ax, Beauty, and Seven Stars—to illustrate the weight of unified taxes and the amount of profits:

Note: This table is from the Ta Kung Pao, September 5, Year 24 (1935)

This table reveals two facts: first, foreign cigarettes are taxed less heavily (with the upper-class Clic being the lightest); and second, foreign cigarettes have higher profits. The Chinese people must think carefully about these relationships. (End)

1940 World Olympic Games May Be Held in Tokyo

Rumors of approval by the International Committee are inaccurate.

(Havas Agency, Berlin, 5th) According to the Nowegian capital's evening newspaper, German news reported that the International Olympic Committee has already decided to hold the 1940 Olympic Games in Tokyo, Japan. Now we know this statement is not accurate, the committee has not yet taken any decision to this day, however the selection of Tokyo is still possible. According to what is known by the interviewer for this newspaper, there has long been talk of holding the 1940 Olympic Games in Tokyo.

(Nowegian Capital, Havas Agency 5th) The International Arimbeik Committee decided here today to hold the World Arimbeik Games in Japan in 1940, a decision that was postponed from last year to today due to the fact that Italy and Japan both want to hold the Arimbeik Games in 1940.

Shanghai Basketball Association: Tung Wah Overpowers Mayling

51 to 43 from the start, always ahead; Tonight at 8 PM, Zhenru faces Pirates

Yesterday's three basketball matches of the Shanghai Basketball Association were all important. In the B Division, Liangxi played against Xiaguang, a crucial match for championship points. The Artillery Team and Eagle Team were also related to future progress. Finally, Tung Wah, with the efforts of all its players, defeated the strong Mayling, which was no easy feat. Tonight, Zhenru will face Pirates in what is expected to be a fierce competition. The details of yesterday's match are recorded below:

Tung Wah Defeats Mayling: As the two teams lined up, the whistle blew, and the battle began. Griffin, weaving through the two-three zone, was the first to score. Tung Wah's Chen Xianglong, unseen for a long time, was still as valiant as ever, receiving assistance from both sides and making two shots out of two. New player Chen Zhongyu made his debut and proved to be extraordinary. Newly selected World Games representatives Feng Nianhua and veteran Lu Zhongen, as forwards, launched subtle attacks, forming a perfect combination and earning cheers from all around as the score rapidly increased. Mayling, known for its fierce attacks, found it difficult to defeat Tung Wah, which combined flexibility and strength. After twenty minutes of play, Tung Wah was far ahead with a score of 30 to 12.

After a ten-minute break, the game resumed. Mayling's captain, Blythe, made a valiant effort, shooting diagonally from close range, scoring three consecutive points. Griffin added another point. Feng Nianhua and Chen urgently caught up, presenting "robes and horses" [gifts for talent]. Blythe, being greedy for the advantage, gradually narrowed the gap. At 26 to 31, the difference was only five points, which was the closest margin of the entire match. After that, Tung Wah's Feng, Chen, Sun, and Lu, probed and attacked from all sides, each showing their skills. In a short time, they surged further ahead. Mayling then launched a fierce attack, but Tung Wah was rich in experience and used looping passes to slow down their attacks, maintaining the lead until the end of the game. Tung Wah won with a score of 51 to 43.
